Welcome to the world of sportscars

Overview

The debut of the Le Mans Prototype in 1999 marked the start of the modern era of sportscar racing, with the new cars being able to race not only at the 24h of Le Mans, but also in a new championship series in America using the same regulations from the ACO. Further series in Europe and Asia were initially planned and some became reality, leading to the creation of the FIA World Endurance Championship in 2012. This led to the demise of the top class in America, but after the creation of the Le Mans Hypercar in 2021 and LMDh in 2023 the top class of sportscar racing is again shared across championships both in Europe and America.



The Cars

Due to the nature of the regulations, allowing manufacturers to develop road-relevant technologies several brands have built top-class sportscars to prove their strength and technology on the world stage. Other constructors have also built cars allowing them to compete against world-class manufacturers both as factory operations and in the hands of privateer teams. The following are a list of cars from every manufacturer factory team as well as every car from constructors opering their cars themselves.


  • BMW
    Car: BMW V12 LMR
    Engine: 6.0L V12 Naturally Aspirated
    Ruleset: LMP900
    Designed by Williams F1

    Last Event: 2000 Las Vegas
    Evolution of the 1998 V12 LM

    Car: Audi R8R

    Engine: 3.6L V8 Twin-turbo

    Last Event: 1999 Le Mans

    Engine: 3.6L V8 Twin-turbo
    Ruleset: LMP900

    First Event: 2000 Sebring

    First Event: 2006 Sebring
    Last Event: 2008 Laguna Seca

Before 1999

As Group C died out in the early 90s, leading to the end of the World Sportscar Championship at the end of 1992 and the GTP class being replaced in the IMSA GT championship after 1993, the top class increasingly consisted of smaller, slower open-cockpit prototypes with production based engines called the World Sports Car (WSC). These were only moderately successful, leading ACO to open up the top class at Le Mans both to older Group C cars, but also allowing GT cars to be able to fight for the overall win as part of the new LMGT1 class. In 1995 the top class became available only to WSC-cars, but the LMGT1 regulations were kept the same. What manufacturers realised was that the GT1 regulations were so open that they could basically build a bespoke prototype and only make 1 road-going version to be able to race. This was first exploited in 1994 when Dauer modified a Porsche 962C and created a single roadcar, allowing them to take the overall win with the Dauer 962. McLaren teamed up with BMW to create the McLaren F1 GTR, which took the overall win in 1995. Meanwhile Porsche, together with TWR and Joest Racing won with a WSC car in 1996 and 1997, several new manufacturers were building new GT1 cars specifically for Le Mans. Porsche entered the 911 GT1 in 1996, Nissan and Panoz debuted the R391 GT1 and Esperante GTR-1 in 1997, and in 1998 Toyota joined with their purpose-built GT-One together with Mercedes with its CLK-LM. At this point the open nature of the regulations were becoming ridiculous, with manufacturers building cars specifically for this class because they only needed to produce a single road-going model. Since these were supposed to be GT cars, the regulations specified that they needed boot space capable of holding a standard size suitcase. Mercedes had placed this space underneath the rear bodywork in a very impractical place, while Toyota managed to convince the scrutineers that because the fuel tank of the GT-One was empty during scrutineering, it could theoretically fit the required space. The by now complete disregard for the intention of the regulations, combined with Mercedes wiping the field clean in the newly created FIA GT Championship to the extent that nobody else entered the class in 1999, the FIA were forced to drop the class and rethink the class-structure at Le Mans. This lead to the creation of the Le Mans Prototype (LMP) and the Le Mans Grand Touring Prototype (LMGTP). Cars in the old LMGT1 class could be modified to fit in the LMGTP class for closed cockpit prototypes, while the LMP class was for open cockpit cars. The LMGT1 class was dropped, with the former LMGT2 class being renamed LMGTS as the top GT class, with GT3-spec cars being eligible in the new LMGT class. With the introduction of these new cars, the ACO looked for opportunities to create a championship with Le Mans-style regulations. After a change of ownership led to IMSA being rebranded as Professional Sports Car Racing (PSCR) in 1997 and a split leading to the creation of Grand-Am and the US Road Racing Championship and the loss of two of its key events, Don Panoz went together with PSCR to partner with the ACO to launch the American Le Mans series for 1999, first testing the format by creating the first edition of the Petit Le Mans at the newly updated Road Atlanta in 1998. After the success of the first running the event, the American Le Mans Series was launched in 1999 with ACO's new class structure, spearheaded by the new LMP and LMGTP classes seeing multiple interested factory teams. For the ACO this was just the start, planning more series running Le Mans regulations both in Europe and Asia.



1999 Season

Overview:

Following the class restructuring from the ACO, teams running in the old LMGT1 class had a choice of class for 1999. Mercedes took the CLK-LM and updated it to LMGTP regulations, becoming the CLR. Toyota did the same, requiring only minor updates to their GT-One.
Nissan chose to modify the R390 to become the open-cockpit R391 for the LMP-class. All three decided to focus purely on Le Mans, with neither bringing their cars to the ALMS.
Porsche started work on a new car for the LMP-class. The LMP2000 was initially supposed to debut in 1999, but discussions over which engine to use delayed the project to 2000, and then it was cancelled in the spring of 1999 due to internal politics.
BMW modified their V12 LM from 1998 built for the previous year's LMP regulations into the V12 LMR to race in the new LMP class, bringing the cars to Sebring for the ALMS season opener, and competing in the remaining races after Le Mans.
Audi joined the sportscar scene with two newly developed cars, the R8R for the LMP class, and the R8C for the LMGTP class. The R8R was designed and built by Dallara in Italy and operated with the help of Joest Racing, whereas the R8C was designed by Racing Technology Norfolk in the UK and operated by Audi Sport Team UK.
Audi brought the R8R to Sebring as preparation for Le Mans, but didn't compete in any other races that season. With the developement of the R8C starting later, that car was only sent to Le Mans.
Panoz also designed the new LMP-1 Roadster-S, a front-engined open-cockpit LMP based on the old Esperante GTR-1. It debuted at the second ALMS race at Road Atlanta and then completed the rest of the season in addition to Le Mans.
For the inaugural season of the ALMS an 8-race calendar was announced, including the season opening 12h of Sebring and the 2nd running of the Petit Le Mans, with other events around circuits in North America as well as a new street race in San Diego to finish the season.
As part of the process of expanding sportscar racing across the world, the ACO planned a non-championship Le Mans-style race in Japan to gauge the interest in Asia for an ALMS-type series. Toyota and Nissan both sent a car each to the race, but neither of the other teams chose to compete there.

The event marred by three airborne accidents and subsequent withdrawal of Mercedes, with the #4 not taking the start after taking off first during practice and then again in the Saturday morning warm-up, and the #5 spectacularly taking off on Saturday evening. The remaining #6 was then withdrawn. Toyota were the favourites to win, but the team struggled with explosive punctures, #1 retiring on Saturday evening, and the #2 crashing out heavily during the night. The #3 was catching the leader towards the end of the race, but suffered another puncture in the last hour, ending the race in 2nd. BMW didn't have the fastest car, but they took the lead by having to pit less often for fuel, and having fewer mechanical issues. #17 was on couse to win but crashed out on Sunday with just a few hours to go, handing the lead and the win to the #15. Nissan and Panoz struggled with reliability, while Audi didn't have the ultimate pace, but good reliability meant the two R8Rs finished 3rd and 4th

    Overall Winner: #23 Nissan Motorsports, Nissan R391, Erik Comas(FRA), Satoshi Motoyama(JAP), Masami Kageyama(JAP), 5:32.56,125

Although Toyota had the advantage on pace, Nissan was able to double-stint the tyres and thus controlled the middle part of the race. However #1 Toyota was reducing the gap until the car failed to start after a scheduled stop during the 3rd hour, dropping it 3 laps down on the leading #23 Nissan as the team changed the battery. #1 Toyota kept trying to fight back, but another penalty after overtaking before the line at a safety car restart during the 5th hour cost it another lap. #23 Nissan thus controlled the pace to take the win, with #1 Toyota eventually finishing 1 lap down in 2nd.

Season Totals:

Number of Races: 10
Total Distance Covered: 12177.746 km



2000 Season

Overview:

After the scary accidents suffered by the Mercedes' at Le Mans was found to be because of a fundamental aerodynamic instability of the car, the team withdrew from racing and the CLRs never raced again.
Nissan and Toyota both also withdrew from sportscars at the end of the year, with Toyota planning to enter F1.
BMW entered F1 in 2000, thus the team didn't return to Le Mans for 2000. However Team Schnitzer continued racing the cars with factory support for the full ALMS Season.
After getting up to speed in 1999, Audi revealed the open cockpit R8 derived from the R8R. The team planned a full season of ALMS, but with the new cars going back to Europe to prepare for Le Mans, the R8R was brought back to complete the events at Charlotte and Silverstone. The closed cockpit R8C was found to be less preferable to the open cockpit design, and thus shelved at the end of the season.
Cadillac joined with the new Northstar LMP with the chassis designed and built by Riley & Scott, the car debuting in the Grand-Am sanctioned 24h of Daytona. Riley & Scott operated the cars as Team Cadillac in selected ALMS races, with french team DAMS operating the cars in the Sports Racing World Cup.
Ascari launched the A410, competing at the European ALMS-rounds in addition to the Sports Racing World Cup, but the team debuted too late to get an entry for Le Mans.
ACO again restructured the classes for Le Mans, renaming the previous year's LMP class LMP900, and adding the LMP675-class for smaller, lighter prototypes. The prototypes running under Grand Am rules and the FIA Sportscar Championship rules could be modified to run in either class. The 900/675-designation refers to the minimum weight of the cars, 900 kg for the top class, 675 kg for the other.
ALMS revealed an expanded calendar for 2000, including new events at Charlotte and Texas. Following the the postponement of the San Diego Race in 1999 it was added as the season opener in 2000. Three overseas races were also included on the calendar, two of them later revealed to be Silverstone and Nurburgring in Europe, and the Race of a Thousand Years on New Year's Eve in Adelaide, Australia. All three were set to launch separate Le Mans Series' in 2001.
Despite the luke warm interest at the 1000km event at Fuji, the ACO scheduled another edition to give it another try.

  5. 68e 24 Heures du Mans
    Circuit de la Sarthe, Le Mans, France
    Date: 17-18.06.2000
    Series: Standalone event
    Race Format: 24 Hours
    Classes: LMP900, LMP675, LMGTS, LMGT
    Circuit Length: 13.605 km
    Laps Completed: 368
    Distance Covered: 5006,640 km
    Number of cars entered: 48 (20 LMP900, 6 LMP675, 10 LMGTS, 12 LMGT)
    Number of cars finished: 27 (12 LMP900, 2 LMP675, 7 LMGTS, 6 LMGT)
    Pole Position: #9 Audi Sport Team Joest, Audi R8, Allan McNish(GBR), Stephane Ortelli(MON), Laurent Aiello(FRA), 3.36,124
    Overall Winner: #8 Audi Sport Team Joest, Audi R8, Frank Biela(DEU), Emanuele Pirro(ITA), Tom Kristensen(DEN), 24:00.00,000
    LMGTS Winner: #51 Viper Team Oreca, Dodge Viper GTS-R, Dominique Dupuy(FRA), Olivier Beretta(MON), Karl Wendlinger(AUT), +35 Laps
    LMGT Winner: #73 Team Taisan Advan, Porsche 911 GT3-R, Hideo Fukuyama(JAP), Atsushi Yogo(JAP), Bruno Lambert(BEL), +58 Laps
    LMP675 Winner: #32 Multimatic Motorsports, Lola B2K/40 - Nissan, Scott Maxwell(CAN), John Graham(CAN), Greg Wilkins(CAN), +94 Laps
    Audi locked out the first 3 places in qualifying with #9 on pole as #11 Panoz completed the 2nd row. The trio of Audis controlled the start as #4 Cadillac retired just 15 minutes in after catching fire, triggering an early safety car. The leaders took the opportunity to make their first stop, with #11 Panoz taking the lead after stopping first ahead of #9 and #7 Audi. #11 controlled the restart as the race entered the 2nd hour, but #9 kept the pressure on and eventually took the lead with #7 soon following it through. #2 Cadillac went off and hit the wall later in the 2nd hour, the car limped back to the pits and went into the garage to repair the damage. #9 and #7 battled for the lead as the race entered its 3rd hour, and as they cycled through the pits #7 took fuel only and rejoined in the lead. Safety car later in the 3rd hour saw the leaders stop again, this time #9 took fuel only and retook the lead. Drama in the 4th hour as #9 spun out and hit the wall, however it rejoined without losing the lead. later in the same hour #8 suffered a puncture and was forced to limp back to the pits, losing 3rd to #11. Into the 5th hour and #1 Cadillac suffered a puncture, causing extensive damage and sending the car into the garage for lengthy repairs. The leaders pitted at the end of the 6th hour, this time #7 rejoined ahead. Into the 7th hour and #2 Cadillac had a lengthy visit to the garage to repair some bent suspension. Drama at the end of the 7th hour as a gearbox issue sent #9 Audi into the garage with the team replacing the entire rear end, rejoining only 4 minutes later in 4th overall. However as #11 made its next stop #9 moved back to 3rd. #8 Audi suffered a puncture during the 9th hour, but managed to limp back and rejoin without losing 2nd. As the race reached 9 hours #9 suffered damage to the diffuser, making several stops for repairs and handing 3rd back to #11 Panoz. Into the 11th hour #7 Audi suffered a puncture and pitted from the lead, with suspension damage forcing the car into the garage for a new rear end. As #8 cycled to the lead #11 Panoz pitted from 3rd and went into the garage with gearbox issues, dropping down the order with lengthy repairs. The issues for #11 meant #7 was left in 3rd, ahead of #12 Panoz in 4th. However at the end of the 11th hour #12 went into the garage with its own gearbox issues. As #11 rejoined during the 12th hour an oil leak forced the car back to the garage again immediately, spending several hours in the garage trying to fix the problems. As the race reached the half way point #12 went off and got stuck in the gravel. The issues for Panoz meant #3 Cadillac cycled up to 3rd ahead of #7, but was soon relegated to 4th. Meanwhile in the 14th hour #1 Cadillac rejoined after several hours following the puncture, but a power steering failure forced it back in for more lengthy repairs before the gearbox failed exiting the pit lane. More gearbox woes for #12 sent the car back to the garage in the 16th hour, #2 Cadillac also joined it in the garage with similar issues. As the Audis cycled through the pits as the race reached 16 hours they took the opportunity to change the brakes, with #7 also forced to bleed the system. Into the 18th hour and problems struck all three remaining Cadillacs, #2 suffered more clutch issues and went back to the garage, #3 suffered a clutch failure and a water leak, and #1 also came back to the garage with more gearbox problems. With the race entering its final 4 hours #3 suffered a suspension failure and was forced to drag the car almost a full lap back to the pits, causing substantial damage. The lengthy repairs handed 4th to #16 Pescarolo Courage. Drama for #11 Panoz just over 1 hour before the end, a puncture sent the car off the road at high speed, but managing to limp back to the pits for repairs before continuing. The Audis cruised through since Sunday morning to secure a 1-2-3, with #8 making its final stop 30 min from the end on the way to the win, with #9 and #7 following it home.

Season Totals:

Number of Races: 13
Total Distance Covered: 14064.568 km



2001 Season

Overview:

After not making the trip to Australia with their prototypes, BMW retired their V12 LMRs, and for 2001 they competed in the GT class with the new V8-powered M3 GTR.
Audi continued racing in ALMS alongside Le Mans with two factory cars, in addition they also sold customer cars to Champion Racing in ALMS and Johansson Motorsport in ELMS.
Panoz competed with the new LMP07 after debuting it at Adelaide the previous year, planning another attack on the ALMS and Le Mans.
Cadillac continued with an upgraded Northstar LMP01, focusing purely on Le Mans with 2 cars operated by DAMS, with Team Cadillac returning to the US to compete in selected ALMS events.
Bentley debuted the closed-cockpit EXP Speed 8 at Le Mans, reviving the LMGTP class which had no entrants in 2000.
After increased interest in the MG-brand, the company set out to compete at Le Mans. The team tasked Lola with building the chassis and AER stood for the engine, with the team selecting the new LMP675 class to compete in, hoping the light weight would give them an advantage against the other factory prototypes.
Ascari continued into their 2nd season, competing again in the FIA Sportscar Championship, in addition to also taking trips to the ELMS round at Donington and Le Mans.
The dominant Dodge Vipers were retired from the GTS class as Chrysler started developement of a brand new LMP-car together with Oreca and Dallara. The new car debuted at the Donington ELMS-race, before the factory effort went to Le Mans.
After debuting at Le Mans in 2000, ALMS took on the LMP900 and LMP675 classes as well in place of the general LMP-class used in 1999 and 2000.
After staging two races in Europe in 2000, ALMS organizer Professional Sports Car Racing was looking to expand and the ELMS was launched as a sister series in Europe, with 5 races across Europe including a 1000km event at Estoril. The calendar also contained optional races at Sebring and Petit Le Mans with ALMS, and the race in Adelaide with APLMS.
The APLMS were also scheduled to start in 2001 following the Race of a Thousand Years at the end of 2000, with Adelaide returning alongside a new event at the Sepang International Circuit in Malaysia.
ALMS presented a new calendar for 2001 centered around the shared events at Donington and Jarama with ELMS and Adelaide and Malaysia with the APLMS. The calendar also contained a new event at a newly upgraded Mont-Tremblant in Canada.
Plans were announced in September 1999 to build a new race track in Aruba. The organizer had an agreement to host the ALMS season opener in 2001, however the 4.345 km Aruba International Raceway was never built due to a conflict between the track promoter and the Aruban government over funding and the event was never officially on the 2001 calendar, with the calendar slot created for the event eventually given to Texas. The failure to comply with the agreements made with ALMS and other series it was supposed to host the organizer ended up mired in legal cases, which the Aruban government eventually lost after shutting down the plans.

  5. 69e 24 Heures du Mans
    Circuit de la Sarthe, Le Mans, France
    Date: 16-17.06.2001
    Series: Standalone event
    Race Format: 24 Hours
    Classes: LMP900, LMGTP, LMP675, LMGTS, LMGT
    Circuit Length: 13.605 km
    Laps Completed: 321
    Distance Covered: 4367.205 km
    Number of cars entered: 48 (18 LMP900, 2 LMGTP, 8 LMP675, 9 LMGTS, 11 LMGT)
    Number of cars finished: 20 (5 LMP900, 1 LMGTP, 2 LMP675, 4 LMGTS, 8 LMGT)
    Pole Position: #2 Audi Sport Team Joest, Audi R8, Laurent Aiello(FRA), Rinaldo Capello(ITA), Christian Pescatori(ITA), 3.32,429
    Overall Winner: #1 Audi Sport Team Joest, Audi R8, Frank Biela(DEU), Emanuele Pirro(ITA), Tom Kristensen(DEN), 24:08.05,892
    LMGTP Winner: #8 Team Bentley, Bentley EXP Speed 8, Andy Wallace(GBR), Butch Leitzinger(USA), Eric van de Poele(BEL), +15 Laps
    LMP675 Winner: #38 ROC Auto, Reynard 2KQ-LM - Volkswagen, Jordi Gene(ESP), Jean-Denis Deletraz(CHE), Pascal Fabre(FRA), +37 Laps
    LMGT Winner: #83 Seikel Motorsport, Porsche 911 GT3-RS, Gabrio Rosa(ITA), Fabio Babini(ITA), Luca Drudi(ITA), +38 Laps
    LMGTS Winner: #63 Corvette Racing, Chevrolet Corvette C5-R, Ron Fellows(CAN), Scott Pruett(USA), Johnny O'Connell(USA), +43 Laps
    #2 Audi qualified on pole and controlled the start ahead of sister #2, as #3 Champion Audi had a terrible start and dropped down the order. #9 Holland Dome went from 4th to 2nd, as #16 Chrysler briefly took 3rd before #1 fought back, with #7 Bentley then demoting the Chrysler to 5th. Heavy rain arrived 15 min into the race with #4 Johansson Audi and #5 Cadillac going off, and a pileup brought out the safety car. Some of the leaders pitted for wets, but #2 Audi stayed out along with #11 Panoz and #9 Dome. However #2 then went off and had to pit with damage, and #9 also elected to stop for wets. #12 Panoz and #34 MG also had to pit for repairs after going off. By the time everyone had cycled through it was #7 Bentley leading ahead of #1 Audi and #11 Panoz, but as the race restarted and the track started drying, the slick-shod #11 took 2nd from from #1. After trading places in the wet and drying sections #11 started catching the leading #7 Bentley. Into the 2nd hour and the leaders pitted with #1 taking inters and #11 and #7 taking fuel only. #11 Panoz rejoined in the lead but #1 soon caught it and took the lead as #33 MG gradually cycled up to 4th and was catching #7 for 3rd. #1 pitted from the lead for slicks and handed the lead to #11 as #34 MG pitted with electrical issues and then a cracked exhaust. #12 Panoz lost a wheel and limped back to the garage as #11 pitted and handed the lead to #7 which was rapidly being caught by #1 before taking the lead. #33 then pitted from 3rd and was delayed after going off entering the pits, with #2 taking the place before taking 2nd from #7. Approaching the 2 hour mark #11 lost a wheel and limped back to the pits, with #12 also pitting as a precaution while the team diagnosed the problem. As the race entered the 3rd hour rain started falling again as #12 returned to the garage with brake issues and #2 slowed and lost 2nd to #7. As #1 and #8 cycled through the pits #3 Champion Audi moved past the Bentley into 4th and #2 moved back past #7 for 2nd. As the rain intensified #4 Johansson Audi stopped on track and retired with electrical issues as the leaders stopped for wets before the safety car came out, with #7 cycling to 2nd ahead of #2 and #8. As the race restarted into the 4th hour both Panoz' pitted and went into the garage with gearbox issues, and #2 Audi took 2nd from #7 Bentley. #6 Cadillac pitted after losing a wheel and went into the garage for suspension repairs. Heavy rain into the 5th hour as #7 pitted and handed 3rd to #3 Champion Audi ahead of #15 Chrysler as #34 MG aquaplaned off before stopping on track and retiring with engine issues. #5 Cadillac then hit problems, going off the track twice before losing a wheel and limping back to the pits for repairs. Drama as #7 Bentley stopped on track and retired with engine failure. Meanwhile #5 Cadillac was back in the garage with more bodywork and suspension damage. Rain continued to fall with several cars suffering minor issues caused by water in the electrics, and around the 6h mark #33 MG pitted with a misfire and went into the garage, with #12 Panoz stopping on track shortly after, before returning to the pits after 30 min and retired with electrical issues. In the meantime sister #11 had also retired after an accident. Problems then hit #3 Champion Audi as it stopped on track and retired from 3rd with electrical issues, with #8 Bentley cycling up behind the factory Audis. Into the 8th hour and problems struck several cars as #8 pitted to check the engine compartment, #16 Chrysler took 3rd before pitting with a water pump failure, #17 Pescarolo Courage cycled to 3rd before going into the garage with engine issues and #33 pitted with broken headlights. The MG eventually retired with a broken oil tank. That left #8 back in 3rd, before gearbox issues forced it back into the pits in the 9th hour, leaving #15 Chrysler 3rd. Drama early in the 11th hour as #2 Audi went into the garage, the team changing the rear end before rejoining, but the comfortable gap to #15 allowed it to maintain 2nd. The Chrysler then pitted and after a long stop the car retired with engine failure, leaving #8 Bentley back in 3rd. As the race entered the 12th hour the track finally started to dry after several hours of persistent rain. #20 Ascari had gradually moved up the standings as cars fell out, but approaching the half way point the car stopped on track and retired. As the race entered its 14th hour #6 Cadillac pitted from 4th and went into the garage with starter motor issues, another unscheduled stop later handing 4th to #16 Chrysler. After spending in excess of 6 hours to repair the car #21 Ascari finally retired in the 16th hour due to the damage sustained earlier. Small issues plagued #2 Audi, an off in the 12th hour where it had to get towed out of the gravel, and a puncture early in the 17th hour, but the car maintained 2nd with a big gap back to #8. More issues struck leading runners across Sunday morning as #16 went into the garage, handing 4th to #6 Cadillac before that suffered a series of starter motor failures over the next few hours, dropping back down the order. Into the 21st hour as the leading #1 Audi went into the garage for a new rear end before rejoining still in the lead. Rain came and went in the closing hours as #6 stopped on track with clutch failure with an hour to go, only to wake up and limp to the finish as #1 Audi cruised home to take the win ahead of sister #2 and #8 Bentley.

Season Totals:

Number of Races: 14
Total Distance Covered: 13497.302 km



2002 Season

Overview:

Audi and Panoz continued their programs in ALMS, with Panoz debuting the LMP01 Evo, an updated version of the LMP-1 Roadster-S following the previous year's flawed LMP07. Panoz' and Audis also competed in the hands of privateer teams, Audi with Champion Racing, and Panoz with several teams, of note MBD who used the discarded LMP07s fitted with Mugen engines.
Cadillac continued their program racing at Le Mans as well as a partial ALMS season, debuting their new Northstar LMP02 with an all new chassis, after abandoning their previous iteration of the Riley & Scott chassis. The manufacturer also cut the ties to DAMS, running the car exclusively under the Team Cadillac banner.
Bentley continued racing at Le Mans with the EXP Speed 8 whilst developing a new car for 2003.
After unreliability plagued the effort in 2001, MG returned to Le Mans with a modified car to improve durability. The team also started selling the car to customers, racing both in ALMS and Le Mans.
Ascari shipped their cars over to the US and renamed it the KZR-1, competing in selected races like the Rolex 24 at Daytona and Sebring, before competing in Le Mans. The team also intended to race in Washington DC, but never made it there.
After finishing the project with Cadillac, Riley & Scott launced a new version of the MK III in 2001, and offered it to customers for the first year. After the bankruptcy by Reynard who owned R&S, the project was taked over by Riley Technologies and for 2002 the factory team was relaunced together with Jim Matthews Racing. They debuted at Sebring before contesting Le Mans and finishing the season with the two last ALMS rounds.
After building the C60 in 2000, for 2002 Courage joined as a factory team, competing in the FIA Sportscar Championship and Le Mans, whilst also supporting its customer Pescarolo.
After joining the prototype field in 2001 Chrysler changed their mind after the season and withdrew from sportscars. Dallara took over the cars and sold them to customers, with Oreca continuing as a privateer.
BMW meanwhile announced in January the cancellation of its ALMS GT program with the M3 GTR after rule changes for the LMGT category limiting its competitiveness of the controversial V8 engine.
At the end of 2001 the ALMS organizer changed its name from Professional Sports Car Racing to bring back the famous IMSA name it had held previously, until a change of ownership in 1997.
The ALMS announced an expanded calendar, with new events at Road America, Washington D.C., Trois-Rivieres and Miami, and a move away from rovals that had been on the calendar in the previous years. The calendar was initially announced with longer races, with all races being at least 3-4 hours long, however most events were reverted back to the normal 2h 45min format after input from TV broadcasters.
After completing the final races of the ELMS in 2001 with as few as 14 cars on the grid, the 2002 season was cancelled in december citing the lack of entrants and the unstable nature of the world following the events of 11th of September. Part of the problem was that the ELMS were competing with similar cars to the FIA Sportscar and GT championships, but they had to be modified to compete in the ELMS. That meand few teams chose to compete due to the resources necessary and the impracticality of competing across the different series.
With the planned debut of the APLMS in 2001 hitting trouble with both its first two rounds cancelled for various reasons, the series were abandoned due to lack of interest and also the difficulties with the global situation. The event in Malaysia was rescheduled for 2002, and when the series was abandoned it became an ALMS invitational event.

Season Totals:

Number of Races: 11
Total Distance Covered: 12252,745 km



2003 Season

Overview:

Audi pulled out of sportscar racing after 2002 as a works team, however the cars kept racing for privateer teams. Joest Racing and Champion Racing contested ALMS, With Champion Racing joining Audi Sport Team UK and the Japanese Team Goh at Le Mans.
Panoz also pulled out as a factory team, with its two LMP01s racing under the JML Team Panoz banner in both ALMS and Le Mans, however the ageing cars struggled for pace.
Bentley debuted a new car, the Speed 8, contesting the 12h of Sebring for the first time as well as Le Mans. For the 3rd season the running of the program was split between Racing Team Norfolk which had operated the cars previously, and Joest Racing who was also working with Audi.
After its most successful year of the program, Cadillac elected not to extend the project, and did not return to sportscar racing in 2003. MG too did not continue into 2003, following financial strain on the company after two years where none of their cars reached the finish. However the car lived on in the hands of privateers across the world.
Riley continued its partnership with Jim Matthews Racing, competing at Sebring and Le Mans while Riley started working on new projects.
Courage continued into 2003, racing its C60 against Pescarolo's now upgraded C60 Evo whilst also developing the C65 which debuted at Le Mans in the LMP675 class.
Lister produced its first prototype for 2003, but for the first year chose to focus on Le Mans where the car made its debut, before entering the 1000 km race at Le Mans at the end of the year.
Having run a GMS-designed car in the FIA Sportscar Championship since 2000, for 2003 Automotive Durango constructed their own car. The PM02 again competed in the FIA Sportscar Championship, but this yeat the team also went to Le Mans for the first time.
For 2003 Ascari moved its focus back to Europe, competing in the FIA Sportscar Championship, but they didn't return to Le Mans or ALMS and the program ended following the 2003 season.
ALMS revealed the new calendar for 2003 with a new race in Mexico City, as well as a planned race in Europe in May. However the European race was soon abandoned after a suitable venue couldn't be agreed on. The format of the Road America race was also changed from 500 Miles to the standard 2h 45min.
Meanwhile, two years on from the failed ELMS, ACO tried again to plan its own sportscar championship in Europe. To prepare for this, it set up another experimental race at La Sarthe to check the interest before committing to the new LMES in 2004.

  11. Grand Prix Americas
    Bayfront Park Street Circuit, Miami, Florida
    Date: 27.09.2003
    Series: ALMS
    Race Format: 2 Hours 45 minutes
    Classes: LMP900, LMP675, GTS, GT
    Circuit Length: 1.851 km
    Laps Completed: 157
    Distance Covered: 290.607 km
    Number of cars entered: 37 (6 LMP900, 5 LMP675, 7 GTS, 19 GT)
    Number of cars finished: 24 (5 LMP900, 4 LMP675, 4 GTS, 11 GT)
    Pole Position: #38 ADT Champion Racing, Audi R8, Johnny Herbert(GBR), JJ Lehto(FIN), 0.47,848
    Overall Winner: #38 ADT Champion Racing, Audi R8, Johnny Herbert(GBR), JJ Lehto(FIN), 2:42.06,617
    GTS Winner: #80 Prodrive, Ferrari 550-GTS Maranello, David Brabham(AUS), Darren Turner(GBR), +3 Laps

    GT Winner: #23 Alex Job Racing, Porsche 911 GT3-RS, Lucas Luhr(DEU), Sascha Maassen(DEU), +6 Laps
    The bumpy track surface caused several incidents, with the #37 Intersport crashing during qualifying and could only just be repaired to start from the pit lane, and the #4 Corvette crashed during warm-up and could not take the start. A big bump in the last corner was so bad the organizer went out overnight before the race to try to smoothen it out, as cars were getting airbourne going over it.
    #38 Champion Audi led the early stages until it made its first pit stop, when the car caught fire during refuelling. it was quickly extinguished, and they could continue, but they lost some time and fell behind the #1 Joest Audi which chose to pit later under green, handing the lead back to the Champion car
    #3 Corvette led GTS until it crashed avoiding an LMP675, it broke the radiator and forced it back to the pits where it could only just be fixed to take the finish
    #11 Panoz retired after hitting the wall, causing heavy damage to the rear of the car
    Chaos as rain started to fall in the final 10 minutes of the race, with several cars going off or spinning, and with a thunderstorm approaching the desicion was taken to end the race 3 minutes early
    The premature finish saved the Champion Audi as its early stop meant it was about to run out of fuel after running almost 2 hours on a tank

    The Panoz-cars were running reliably, with the #10 taking 2nd behind the Champion car, while the #11 ended up 4th after suffering with power steering failure

Total Distance Covered: 12880.997 km



2004 Season

Overview:

The ACO announced changes in the class structure for 2004, with LMP900 and LMP675 being replaced by LMP1 and LMP2. LMP900 and LMGTP-cars moved to LMP1, and LMP675 cars could be converted to either of the new classes. Rule changes were also announced for LMP1 with overhang limited and the floor structure changed to limit downforce and make the cars less likely to take off. IMSA announced that they would delay enforcing these new rules in ALMS, allowing both new LMP1 and LMP2 cars and old LMP900 and LMP675 cars to compete in what became the P1 and P2 class. This allowed Dyson racing to continue using their LMP675 MG-Lolas, moving them into the P1 class.
After the announcement of the 1000 km of Le Mans preview race in 2003, ACO launched the new Le Mans Endurance Series, racing on classic European circuits and bringing back the classic 1000 km/6 hour format from the old World Sportscar Championship days. Having learned from the ELMS in 2001, the new series attracted several teams from the FIA Sportscar championship and FIA GT championship, with the lack of interest forcing the FIA Sportscar Championship to end following the 2003 season.
Audi started work on a new car to succeed the R8, which would ultimately debut in 2006. Meanwhile the Joest Team ended their program in ALMS, leaving only Champion Racing competing in the US. In Europe, Team Goh and Audi Sport UK also operated Audis in the new LMES, with Team UK also making the trip to Sebring.
After winning Le Mans in the 3rd year of the program, Bentley ended their sportscar program and didn't return. Panoz too elected not to return in the top class with the LMP01, instead focusing on their GT-class program.
Having originally developed the 02S in 2002, Reynard went bankrupt and International Racing Management took over the project and renamed it the DBA 03S for 2003. In 2004 the production was taken over by Zytek, with the 2003 chassis sold to Creation Autosportif and the new cars were badged as the Zytek 04S and campaigned by the Zytek factory team. Both cars were entered in the LMES, with Zytek only running a limited program while Creation brought the 2003-car to the two final ALMS rounds as well.
Lister went into their 2nd season with the Storm LMP, starting at Le Mans before finishing the LMES season.
Having been a Courage customer for several years, Henri Pescarolo's team took their 2003 car and updated it themselves, improving the aero and switching out the Peugeot engine for a new Judd V10. They debuted the new Pescarolo C60 at Monza, competing in LMES as well as bringing 2 cars to Le Mans.
Meanwhile Courage switched to the LMP2 class to compete with the new C65 that debuted the year before.
With the new LMP1 regulations the R&S MK III C was becoming outdated, and with the factory switching its focus to the Rolex Sportscar Series DP class, the ALMS and Le Mans program was reduced to supporting the remaining customers.
As the new LMP1 regulations made older LMP900 obsolete, Durango switched its focus back to single seaters and didn't return to sportscars in 2004.
ALMS announced their new calendar for 2004, with a focus on making sure all events could be run following cancellations and replacements in the last few years. The calendar included a return to Mid-Ohio and Portland, as well as a new event at Lime Rock Park. Laguna Seca also became the season finale, with the race extended to 4 hours.
For its first season LMES revealed a 4 round calendar across 4 legendary circuits around Europe, visiting Monza, Nurburgring, Silverstone and Spa.

Total Distance Covered: 16229.946 km



2005 Season

Overview:

With the ageing Audi R8 still being competitive, the ACO announced that 2005 would be the last year that cars built to the old LMP900 rules would be permitted to race, and the cars were also handicapped with more ballast and less power than the newer LMP1 machines. Older generation LMP900 cars would still be allowed to race in ALMS, with IMSA not enforcing the new rules yet, allowing older cars to compete alongside newer LMP1 cars.
The FIA and ACO also revised the classes for GT-cars, with LMGTS and LMGT replaced by LMGT1 and LMGT2. The new classes were designed to more tightly control and balance the cars, with specific laptime requirements set. The new structure meant new cars would have to be homologated by the FIA before being allowed to compete.
In the US, Champion Racing continued racing their two R8s, also competing at Le Mans. Audi Sport Team UK and Team Goh chose not to continue beyond 2004, with Team Oreca taking over one of the R8s to compete in the LMES and Le Mans.
After racing the C60 in 2004, Pescarolo updated the car for 2005 to the new hybrid regulations that meant the car avoided the handicaps imposed on the old LMP900 cars. The team raced 1 of the new C60 Hybrids in the LMES, with a 2nd car joining for Le Mans.
Courage's factory team moved back to LMP1 for 2005, racing an upgraded C60 for the new hybrid regulations.
The Zytek factory team expanded their program for 2005 after new investment from Essex Invest. The team used the 2004-car with the new restrictions from the ACO, competing in the full LMES season as well as selected ALMS races.
With the sponsorship from Essex Invest moving to Zytek, it left Lister with a reduced budget for 2005. The team started at Spa, but by the Silverstone round the team debuted a new Hybrid version of the car in the hope that it would be more competitive.
Porsche announced its return to sportscar racing with the new RS Spyder, built for the LMP2 regulations. Porsche partnered with Penske Motorsport to run the cars, testing throughout 2005 and initially planning to debut at Petit Le Mans before that was delayed to the final round at Laguna Seca.
In the GT-classes, new cars were introduced with the new regulations. Corvette replaced the old C5-R with the new C6.R, and Aston Martin joined with the brand new DBR9. There was also controversy as IMSA allowed Maserati to run in the GT1 clas in ALMS with the MC12, despite the car not being built to LMGT1 spec. The decision drew criticism from ACO and from several of the teams, with Aston Martin protesting the car at the first round in Sebring.
The schedule for the 24h of Le Mans was adjusted after discussions between IMSA and the ACO who were finding it challenging to schedule races early in the season with the mandatory test day being a month before the race forcing both ALMS and LMES to effectively take a long break to allow teams to race at Le Mans. In 2005 the test day was moved to 2 weeks before the race, allowing more flexibility for ALMS to schedule more races early in the season.
IMSA focused on concistency in the ALMS calendar, keeping all events from 2004 as well as adding the return of a sprint event at Road Atlanta. they also took advantage of the Le Mans test day being moved to reschedule Mid-Ohio to May, before Le Mans.
LMES also focused on steady growth after a successful first season, keeping the 4 events from 2004, and adding a fifth round at the new Istanbul Park.

    Pole Position: #16 Pescarolo Sport, Pescarolo C60 Hybrid, Emmanuel Collard(FRA), Jean-Chrisophe Boullion(FRA), Eric Comas(FRA), 3.34,715
    Overall Winner: #3 ADT Champion Racing, Audi R8, JJ Lehto(FIN), Marco Werner(DEU), Tom Kristensen(DEN), 24:01.30,901

    The #4 Team Oreca Audi also suffered issues in the night, twice being rolled into the garage for suspension repairs
    #2 Audi went off again on Sunday morning after a tyre failure, getting stuck in the gravel and then losing more time being repaired in the garage
    #17 Pescarolo suffered a myriad of issues on Sunday morning, ending in retirement after crashing out and suffering extensive damage
    By Sunday lunchtime the #16 Pescarolo was back in 2nd and catching the leading Audi at a pace that it could catch the lead by the end of the race. However, with less that 2h to go it was starting to overheat, with the team briefly rolling it back to the garage to clean the radiators and cruising to 2nd place
    This meant the #3 Champion Audi could control the pace after a flawless run to take the win, with Tom Kristensen taking a record-breaking 7th Le Mans win

    The #2 Audi was penalized for a pit lane infringement at the first stop, then started catching up to the leading Dysons.

Season Totals:

Number of Races: 16
Total Distance Covered: 17184.822 km



2006 Season

Overview:

With the ACO outlawing old LMP900 cars from Le Mans, Audi revealed the R10 TDI to replace the R8. That also coincided with Audi returning as a factory team, cooperating with Champion Racing in ALMS with team Joest running the cars at Le Mans. With IMSA still allowing older cars to compete, it also gave them the opportunity to take a single R8 on a farewell tour over the first few ALMS rounds while the R10s were testing for Le Mans. News also came in 2005 that Peugeot would also join LMP1 in 2007 with their own diesel-powered prototype.
After debuting in the ALMS season finale in 2005, Porsche went into the first full season with the RS Spyder. The team focused on competing solely in ALMS, as the ACO did not welcome factory teams in the LMP2 class at Le Mans.
Pescarolo continued racing in Europe with its C60 Hybrid after a successful 2005-season, again fielding 1 car for the LMS season, and a second car for Le Mans.
Courage debuted a new car, the LC70 and formed a partnership with Mugen who delivered engines for the factory team. The car was also sold to customers.
Zytek continued into their 3rd season, but were forced to update the car for the Hybrid LMP1 rules. The team again competed in the LMS with the updated 06S, before bringing the car across the Atlantic for the final ALMS rounds.
After running the DBA 03S in 2004 and 2005 the Hybrid regulations forced a redesign, the team partnered with KWM to create the CA06/H with the latest Judd engine, completing the LMS, Le Mans and the final two rounds in ALMS.
Lister went into 2006 with plans to complete the full LMS season with the Storm LMP Hybrid, but it announced at Le Mans that development of the car would cease and the team skipped Nurburgring to bring the final updates to Donington.
Giovanni Lavaggi announced his intention to build his own Le Mans prototype and become the first driver-constructor in modern history. The Lavaggi LS1 made its debut at Jarama for the LMS finale.
ALMS released a new calendar, with Sonoma and the spring race at Road Atlanta being replaced by a race at the new Miller Motorsports Park in Utah, and a new street circuit in Houston Texas, run together with Champ Car.
LMES continued with a 5-race calendar with a few shuffled dates, as well as switching the British round from Silverstone to Donington Park. The series also underwent a slight rebranding, and became known simply as the Le Mans Series.
Work conducted by the people behind Team Goh culminated in the debut of the new ACO-backed Japan Le Mans Challenge, organizing 3 1000 km races in Japan, in an effort to get japanese teams interested in international sportscar racing.

    Circuit Length: 6.019 km
    Laps Completed: 349
    Distance Covered: 2100.631 km
    Number of cars entered: 35 (6 P1, 7 P2, 6 GT1, 16 GT2)
    Number of cars finished: 19 (2 P1, 3 P2, 5 GT1, 9 GT2)
    Pole Position: #2 Audi Sport North America, Audi R10 TDI, Rinaldo Capello(ITA), Allan McNish(GBR), Tom Kristensen(DEN), 1.45,828
    Overall Winner: #2 Audi Sport North America, Audi R10 TDI, Rinaldo Capello(ITA), Allan McNish(GBR), Tom Kristensen(DEN), 12:01.56,561
    P2 Winner: #37 Intersport Racing, Lola B05/40 - AER, Jon Field(USA), Clint Field(USA), Liz Halliday(USA), +4 Laps

    Pole sitting #2 Audi suffered issues in the warm-up, and had to start from the pit lane after replacing a heat exchanger before the start. That left #1 on pole, ahead of the two Porsches
    Both Porsches suffered problems in the opening hours with #7 briefly stopping on track, and the #6 was forced into the pits to replace a broken alternator. #7 later had to pit for lengthy repairs to a broken radiator and steering issues
    #1 Audi led the early stages despite a spin after getting confused in traffic with #2 catching up to lie 2nd. However #1 then retired with an overheating engine around the 4 hour mark
    #2 was left alone out front, but it wasn't plain sailing as it suffered issues in the pits at the half way point, struggling to remove a loose wheel as well as having to clean the fuel filter
    The Porsches continued to suffer reliability issues, with #7 retiring with a broken driveshaft 5 hours from the end, and #6 retired in the final hour with an oil leak
    Despite the issues encountered, #2 Audi cruised home to take the win

    An early safety car meant the top 3 made their first stop, leaving #1 leading and #2 emerging first of the pit callers. #1 made its first stop under a later safety car, leaving #2 in the lead
    #6 Porsche suffered a broken throttle sensor during the same SC, causing a lengthy pit stop for repairs
    #16 Dyson made it up to 3rd, but contact in traffic and subsequent penalty dropped it down the order. The Zytek was pressuring the leading #2, and eventually made it past and started to pull away, until pitting during another safety car
    #7 Porsche pitted from the class lead and went straight to the garage with the fuel cell leaking
    Incidents and reliability issues started taking its toll, with #20 Dyson suffering a heavy crash 2.5h into the race, and sister #16 retired with an engine failure just past the 5h mark. The Zytek briefly took the lead during the 7th hour, until a puncture dropped it back down the order. That left the Creation in 3rd, but it then had its own incident, going off on some oil
    Drama as the race reached 9 hours with #1 Audi pitting from 2nd with broken suspension, and retired as there wasn't time to fix it before the finish
    #2 Audi thus took the win ahead of #15 Zytek and one of the ageing MG-Lolas taking 3rd

    Number of cars finished: 21 (5 P1, 5 P2, 4 GT1, 7 GT2)
    Pole Position: #15 Zytek Engineering, Zytek 06S, Johnny Mowlem(GBR), Stefan Johansson(SWE), 1.13,731
    Overall Winner: #2 Audi Sport North America, Audi R10 TDI, Rinaldo Capello(ITA), Allan McNish(GBR), 4:00.45,954
    P2 Winner: #7 Penske Motorsports, Porsche RS Spyder, Romain Dumas(FRA), Lucas Luhr(DEU), +1.03,968

    #15 Zytek and #88 Creation locked out the front row and took the early lead, as the two Audis overtook #6 Porsche which went from 3rd to 5th

    #7 Porsche took the lead when the leading Creation and #2 Audi pitted 1,5h into the race. by the time the Porsche pitted along with #1 it was #2 that emerged in the lead

    #16 Dyson briefly took the lead, however it was soon passed by the Zytek, which then made a critical error pitting just as the safety car came out, when the pits were closed
    #2 Audi also pitted during the safety car to top up with fuel, hoping to stretch it to the end. As the race restarted the Zytek immediately took the lead from #7 Porsche, but pitted to serve the penalty for pitting before the pit entry opened
    The safety car came back out shortly after, allowing #1 to make its final stop with #2 potentially needing a splash to finish the race
    On the restart #2 Audi went from 3rd to the lead, with #7 Porsche 2nd and #16 Dyson losing places to the Creation and #1 as well
    #7 Porsche was pressuring the #2 Audi, but a spin proved costly as well as needing a splash to get to the finish
    #2 was in maximum fuel save, and just about managed to stretch it to the finish to win, with #1 taking 2nd as others around it also had to pit for a splash

Season Totals:

Number of Races: 16
Total Distance Covered: 17202.127 km



2007 Season

Overview:

The big news of the season was Peugeot returning to sportscar racing with the 908 HDi FAP, competing in the Le Mans Series and Le Mans with 2 cars.
Audi continued their program in the ALMS, joined by Porsche who revealed an upgraded evolution of the RS Spyder, however Porsche continuing to focus exclusively on ALMS. The new car was also run by Dyson racing, who replaced the Lolas from 2006, moving down to the P2 class.
Acura joined ALMS with a new factory effort in the P2 class. For the first season they took a Courage LC75 chassis and upgraded it extensively, badging the car as the ARX-01a in the P2 class at Sebring. Two of the teams ran the new car, with the 3rd factory-supported team racing a Lola chassis, focusing purely on engine developement.
A big talking point was the lack of pace difference between the P1 and P2 cars in the ALMS, with IMSA deciding not to follow the ACO in reducing the restrictor diameter by 5% for LMP2 cars, allowing them to be much closer to the P1 Audis on pace.
After winning every LMS race of the season, Pescarolo switched their focus to building a new car themselves, debuting the new Pescarolo 01 at the LMS opener at Monza. 2 factory operated cars completed the LMS season and Le Mans, with several other teams running the car as customers in both LMP1 and LMP2.
Courage continued into the 2nd year with the LC70, but after running Mugen engines the year before, in 2007 they switched to AER powerplants.
With the new LMP1 regulations Zytek had to build an all new chassis, the 07S. After 3 years as a factory team Zytek switched their focus to offering factory support to customer teams operating the new car, with several customers both in LMP1 and LMP2.
Creation Autosportif constructed the new CA07 for the new LMP1 regulations, with the factory team debuting the new car at Le Mans in addition to supporting customers running the car in LMP2.
Lavaggi went into its first full season as a tiny factory operation, intending to compete in the LMS whilst continuing to develop the car.
With the older Hybrid prototypes outlawed and development of the Storm ceased, Lister went into 2007 with the goal of building a new car around the Pescarolo 01. They hired Peter Elleray to lead the aero development team and a switch to Judd engines was planned for the new Lister Judd. However after delays the project was cancelled due to financial issues.
ALMS revealed a revised calendar with 3 new events, racing at street circuits in St. Petersburg and Detroit together with the IRL, and joining Champ Car at Long Beach. The new calendar also saw the event at Road America extended to 4 hours, and the Portland race dropped off the calendar.
The LMS also revealed a modified calendar, returning to Monza and Silverstone, as well as a new event in Valencia in Spain. A 6th event was added later in the form of Interlagos in Brazil, running to 1000 Miles rather than the usual 1000 km distance. The event in Istanbul dropped off the calendar after two years.
After a slow start in 2006, the JLMC planned a steady growth by keeping the 3 races from 2006, and adding a 4th race at Fuji. The hope was that the 2007 season would see more notable entrants and bigger grids compared to the previous season.

    Overall Winner: #2 Audi Sport North America, Audi R10 TDI, Frank Biela(DEU), Emanuele Pirro(ITA), Marco Werner(DEU), 12:01.14,838

    The two Audis led the early laps ahead of #7 Porsche, with #1 taking the lead 15 min in as #2 hit traffic. #6 Porsche suffered brake issues in the first hour and dropped down the order. As the Audis made their first stop #2 was penalized for a pit stop infringement, and then in the 2nd hour suffered a puncture costing it 2 laps limping back to the pits, it was then penalized an hour later for speeding in the pit lane, with #1 was also penalized shortly after for contact in the pit lane with #16 Dyson. That left #7 Porsche in the lead, but it soon pitted with electrical issues, the team initially changing the battery, but the car lost a lot of time in the pits repeatedly for more new batteries and eventually a new alternator cable. #6 Porsche also suffered similar electrical issues and it too dropped a long way down with repeated visits to the pits. #1 Audi pitted for a routine stop at the 5h mark, but failed to start and the car dropped down the order, suffering the same issue multiple times over the following few hours. That left #2 back in the lead after its earlier problems, with the new #26 Acura 2nd overall and #9 Acura 3rd, until #9 slowed with electrical issues, it too dropping down the order. #2 made a routine stop approaching 7h, but was penalized for a pit stop infringement and held for an extra 40s. Following a series of safety cars #26 ended up right behind the leading #2, but over the final few hours it drifted to 6 laps down with multiple stops for small repairs as well as clearing the radiators and refilling gearbox oil, while #2 Audi cruised home to take the win

    LMGT1 Winner: #009 Aston Martin Racing, Aston Martin DBR9, David Brabham(AUS), Darren Turner(GBR), Rickard Rydell(SWE), +26 Laps
    LMGT2 Winner: #76 IMSA Performance Matmut, Porsche 997 GT3-RSR, Richard Lietz(AUT), Patrick Long(USA), Raymond Narac(FRA), +49 Laps

    #7 Peugeot started on pole, but went off in T1 in slightly damp conditions, handing the lead to #2 Audi. #7 eventually fell down to 5th, with the Audis holding the first 3 positions. An early rain shower at the hour mark made conditions difficult, but the leaders stayed on slicks as the rain didn't last long. Drama in the 2nd hour as #3 Audi crashed out, retiring on the spot and causing a lengthy safety car to repair the barrier. Another shower of rain in the 3rd hour saw #7 Peugeot briefly switch to wets, but it proved to be the wrong call as the track dried again, forcing another stop. #8 Peugeot hit problems in the 5th hour and pitted with suspension issues, dropping 8 laps in the garage. #1 Audi was having a steady race in 2nd until contact with #63 Corvette in the 7th hour forcing it to pit to fix some damaged bodywork. #2 Audi dominated and pulled out a substantial lead, but on Sunday morning it dramatically crashed out after losing a wheel and retired on the spot. With just 3h to go #7 Peugeot suffered engine issues, and after trying to repair it in the garage, it too retired from the race. Rain started falling with 2 hours to go, forcing everyone to switch to wets, and as the rain intensified the safety car was deployed in the final hour, with #8 Peugeot being rolled into the garage with a gearbox issue. 10 minutes from the end the safety car pulled in, but #1 Audi comfortably cruised home to take the win, with #8 Peugeot finishing 2nd after stopping and waiting for the finish

Season Totals:

Number of Races: 19
Total Distance Covered: 19778.673 km



2008 Season

Overview:

Audi expanded their program for the third season with the R10, competing in ALMS as well as in the LMS. Peugeot also continued for a full season in LMS, but they also joined ALMS at Sebring and Petit Le Mans.
Pescarolo continued into their 2nd season in the LMS with the 01, the car proving popular amongst customer teams as well, both in LMP1 and LMP2.
In 2007 Oreca bought Courage with the goal to develop a new car for 2009. In 2008 the Oreca team ran 2 modified LC70s badged as Courage-Orecas.
Creation Autosportif went into their 2nd season with the CA07, partnering with AIM to get upgraded Judd engines. The team completed the LMS season and Le Mans with two cars at most events.
A new constructor in the form of Epsilon Euskadi joined with a new car, completing the LMS season and gaining a late 2nd entry for Le Mans.
With the aging S101 having raced successfully with privateers since 2001, Dome built a new car for 2008, the Dome S102. The team brought the car to Le Mans for its debut, hoping to generate interest to sell the car to customers.
After repeated engine failures forced Lavaggi to reduce their program, and for 2008 the team replaced their Ford units with AER twin-turbo V8s. Due to the global financial crisis many of the team's sponsors had left the project and the team was now operating on a shoestring budget. Nevertheless the team continued on, continuing to compete in the LMS.
Porsche continued into their third season in the ALMS with the RS Spyder, with the factory team again focusing exclusively on North America. The team continued to operate 2 cars for the ALMS season, but facing a championship fight against Acura a third car was scrambled with people from the IndyCar crew to help the effort for the final 2 rounds. For the first time privateer teams also brought the RS Spyder to Europe to compete in LMS and at Le Mans.
Following an encouraging first season Acura expanded their program for 2008, with 4 teams using the updated ARX-01b. AGR and Highcroft continue from 2007, with the Fernandez team returning now also with the Acura chassis after competing with a Lola the previous year. The 4th team to join the program was the newly created de Ferran motorsports, debuting in Utah.
Minor changes in the regulations for LMP1 and LMP2 announced by the ACO to further level the performance between petrol and diesel cars, as well as increasing the gap between LMP1 and LMP2. IMSA chose to implement some of these changes, primarily to slow the P2 cars, which dominated large parts of the previous season.
ALMS focused on continuity and revealed a calendar featuring all the events from 2007, with only small adjustments to race lengths.
Meanwhile LMS featured a modified calendar, with the event in Valencia moving to Barcelona, and the overseas round in Brazil removed.
After two dire seasons of the JLMC, with lacklustre grids and few interested teams, the series was cancelled after the ACO briefly took control of it, with the focus instead shifting to create a new series known as the Asian Le Mans Series, with an test event planned in Shanghai at the end of the year.

Calendar:

  1. 56th Annual Mobil 1 12 Hours of Sebring
    Sebring International Raceway, Sebring, Florida
    Date: 15.03.2008
    Series: ALMS
    Race Format: 12 Hours
    Classes: P1, P2, GT1, GT2
    Circuit Length: 6.019 km
    Laps Completed: 351
    Distance Covered: 2112.669 km
    Number of cars entered: 34 (5 P1, 10 P2, 3 GT1, 16 GT2)
    Number of cars finished: 20 (4 P1, 5 P2, 3 GT1, 8 GT2)
    Pole Position: #1 Audi Sport North America, Audi R10 TDI, Rinaldo Capello(ITA), Allan McNish(GBR), Tom Kristensen(DEN), 1.43,195
    Overall Winner: #7 Penske Motorsports, Porsche RS Spyder Evo, Timo Bernhard(DEU), Romain Dumas(FRA), Emmanuel Collard(FRA), 12:01.39,587
    P1 Winner: #1 Audi Sport North America, Audi R10 TDI, Rinaldo Capello(ITA), Allan McNish(GBR), Tom Kristensen(DEN), +1.07,697
    GT1 Winner: #3 Corvette Racing, Chevrolet Corvette C6.R, Johnny O'Connell(USA), Jan Magnussen(DEN), Ron Fellows(CAN), +23 Laps
    GT2 Winner: #45 Flying Lizard Motorsports, Porsche 997 GT3-RSR, Jörg Bergmeister(DEU), Marc Lieb(DEU), Wolf Henzler(DEU), +37 Laps
    #1 Audi qualified on pole ahead of #07 Peugeot, with the Peugeot taking the lead at the start. #1 Audi made contact with a GT car in the opening hour, with the leaders pitting under the resulting safety car and #1 was penalized for the incident. #07 Peugeot maintained the lead ahead of #2 Audi and #26 Acura. Problems struck #6 Porsche as the race hit 1h, an oil leak and overheating eventually proving terminal. #2 Audi was pressuring the leading Peugeot, but repeated offs with braking issues costing the car places, and handed the podium places to #26 Acura and #7 Porsche. However by the time the leaders had made their 2nd stop #1 Audi had fought back to take 2nd behind the leading Peugeot. As the race approached 3 hours drama struck #07 Peugeot, pitting from the lead with hydraulic issues and dropping several laps down after multiple lengthy stops do fix a broken hydraulic pump. The two Audis took over the lead, until #2 pitted with a turbo failure as the race reached half way, and with #1 too pitting shortly after the #7 Porsche resumed the lead. Problems for #1 Audi started to show itself as the race went into its 8th hour, making a lengthy stop to repair a bent suspension arm, and later stopping again to replace the front brakes. #26 Acura was trying to fight back after pace struggles and a timing error resulting in a lengthy safety car, until a stop in the 8th hour with water temperature issues proved costly. #2 Audi was mired in bad luck, a brief off in the 10th hour forced it to pit for bodywork repairs. #07 Peugeot was recovering from its earlier delays, until a wheel bearing issue in the 11th hour delayed it again. At the same time #26 Acura pitted and retired, with the water temperature issues proving terminal. #7 Porsche controlled the closing hours of the race to take the win, with #15 Acura initially finishing 2nd until a broken airbox resulted in the car being disqualified. That promoted #20 Dyson to 2nd, with #1 Audi taking the final podium position

  2. Acura Sports Car Challenge of St. Petersburg
    Streets of St. Petersburg, St. Petersburg, Florida
    Date: 05.04.2008
    Series: ALMS
    Race Format: 1 Hour 55 minutes
    Classes: P1, P2, GT1, GT2
    Circuit Length: 2.910 km
    Laps Completed: 81
    Distance Covered: 235.710 km
    Number of cars entered: 29 (3 P1, 9 P2, 3 GT1, 14 GT2)
    Number of cars finished: 21 (1 P1, 8 P2, 2 GT1, 10 GT2)
    Pole Position: #2 Audi Sport North America, Audi R10 TDI, Marco Werner(DEU), Lucas Luhr(DEU), 1.02,825
    Overall Winner: #2 Audi Sport North America, Audi R10 TDI, Marco Werner(DEU), Lucas Luhr(DEU), 1:55.33,690
    P2 Winner: #7 Penske Motorsports, Porsche RS Spyder Evo, Timo Bernhard(DEU), Romain Dumas(FRA), +0,818
    GT1 Winner: #4 Corvette Racing, Chevrolet Corvette C6.R, Oliver Gavin(GBR), Olivier Beretta(MCO), +2 Laps
    GT2 Winner: #71 Tafel Racing, Ferrari F430 GT, Dirk Müller(DEU), Dominik Farnbacher(DEU), +4 Laps
    #2 Audi qualified on pole, ahead of #7 Porsche and #9 Acura. The start was delayed after #007 broke down and forcing an extra formation lap. #2 Audi controlled the lead at the start ahead of #7 Porsche as #26 Acura barged its way into 3rd, until a costly spin in the early laps dropped it a lap down. The leaders made their first stop under safety car after 45min, with #7 Porsche taking only fuel and gaining track position ahead of #2 Audi. #1 Audi had a lengthy stop, replacing the rear end and dropping a lap down. Another safety car 1h 10min in saw #1 Audi and #6 Porsche make a 2nd stop for tyres, both down the order after earlier issues. The leaders stayed out, all able to go the distance on just 1 stop. On the restart #2 Audi pressured #7 and muscled its way into the lead, as #15 Acura and #1 Audi made contact, #15 going off and #1 forced to pit with damage which proved terminal. #7 Porsche fought back to re-take the lead as #2 got stuck in traffic, as another incident prompted another late-race safety car. The race finally restarted with 2 min left, and #2 Audi used the mighty torque to take the lead and won the race ahead of #7, with #9 Acura finishing 3rd despite late pressure from #6 Porsche

  3. 1000 km de Catalunya
    Circuit de Catalunya, Montmelo, Spain
    Date: 06.04.2008
    Series: LMS
    Race Format: 1000 km or 6 Hours
    Classes: LMP1, LMP2, LMGT1, LMGT2
    Circuit Length: 4.655 km
    Laps Completed: 215
    Distance Covered: 1000.825 km
    Number of cars entered: 48 (15 LMP1, 15 LMP2, 5 LMGT1, 13 LMGT2)
    Number of cars finished: 34 (11 LMP1, 10 LMP2, 3 LMGT1, 10 LMGT2)
    Pole Position: #8 Team Peugeot Total, Peugeot 908 HDi FAP, Stephane Sarrazin(FRA), Pedro Lamy(POR), 1.31,875
    Overall Winner: #7 Team Peugeot Total, Peugeot 908 HDi FAP, Nicolas Minassian(FRA), Marc Gene(ESP), 5:59.30,812
    LMP2 Winner: #34 Van Merksteijn Motorsport, Porsche RS Spyder Evo, Jos Verstappen(NED), Peter van Merksteijn Sr.(NED), +7 Laps
    LMGT1 Winner: #72 Luc Alphand Adventures, Chevrolet Corvette C6.R, Luc Alphand(FRA), Guillaume Moreau(FRA), Patrice Goueslard(FRA), +21 Laps
    LMGT2 Winner: #96 Virgo Motorsport, Ferrari F430 GT, Robert Bell(GBR), Gianmaria Bruni(ITA), +26 Laps
    Peugeot locked out the front row ahead of #1 Audi. #8 controlled the lead at the start, with the Audi barging its way into 2nd until #7 Peugeot re-took the position after pressuring #1. The leaders made their first stop under safety car, with #1 Audi taking fuel only and cycling to the lead. The Audi maintained the lead throughout the 2nd stint despite intense pressure from the pair of Peugeots, with #8 Moving into 2nd as the race reached the hour mark. Shortly after contact forced #8 Peugeot into the garage for repairs, dropping several laps down. #7 Peugeot had several moments including a brief off trying to catch #1, until the leading Audi pitted with a slow puncture. #1 ended up back in the garage later in the 2nd hour following a broken alternator belt. That left #7 Peugeot in the lead ahead of #2 Audi, with the Peugeot opening up a substantial gap. Problems continued for #8 as the race neared the 4h mark, going back into the garage after contact. #7 Peugeot controlled the closing stages despite concern about damage to the headlight, and it took the win followed by #2 Audi.

  4. Tequila Patron American Le Mans Series at Long Beach
    Long Beach Street Circuit, Long Beach, California
    Date: 19.04.2008
    Series: ALMS
    Race Format: 1 Hour 40 minutes
    Classes: P1, P2, GT1, GT2
    Circuit Length: 3.167 km
    Laps completed: 71
    Distance Covered: 224.857 km
    Number of cars entered: 28 (4 P1, 8 P2, 2 GT1, 14 GT2)
    Number of cars finished: 26 (4 P1, 8 P2, 2 GT1, 12 GT2)
    Pole Position: #7 Penske Motorsports, Porsche RS Spyder Evo, Timo Bernhard(DEU), Romain Dumas(FRA), 1.11,330
    Overall Winner: #2 Audi Sport North America, Audi R10 TDI, Marco Werner(DEU), Lucas Luhr(DEU), 1:40.37,791
    P2 Winner: #9 Patron Highcroft Racing, Acura ARX-01b, Scott Sharp(USA), David Brabham(AUS), Stefan Johansson(SWE), +3,786
    GT1 Winner: #3 Corvette Racing, Chevrolet Corvette C6.R, Johnny O'Connell(USA), Jan Magnussen(DEN), +1 Lap
    GT2 Winner: #71 Tafel Racing, Ferrari F430 GT, Dirk Müller(DEU), Dominik Farnbacher(DEU), +3 Laps
    #7 Porsche qualified on pole ahead of #15 Acura, however it was #6 Porsche taking the lead at the start with #9 Acura also in the mix. #2 Audi was moving up the order, taking 4th from #9, and after an early safety car it took 3rd from #15 and started catching the Porsches. After moving past #7 into 2nd and pressuring the leading #6, #2 Audi made its only stop of the race. #6 Porsche pitted from the lead a few laps later and rejoined comfortably in front. #7 made its stop a lap later, but taking only 2 tyres it emerged ahead of them both, and eventually cycled to the front after the rest of the leaders had pitted. The Audi started fighting back, taking 2nd on the restart and eventually catching and taking the lead from #7 Porsche as they hit traffic. After another safety car #1 Audi was also moving up the order taking 2nd behind sister #2, and they duly controlled the gap to finish 1-2. Meanwhile a later stop under the safety car saw #9 Acura on fresher tyres catching and passing both Porsches in the closing stages do finish 3rd.
