  6. 1000 km di Monza
    Autodromo Nazionale di Monza, Monza, Italy
    Date: 27.04.2008
    Series: LMS
    Race Format: 1000 km or 6 Hours
    Classes: LMP1, LMP2, LMGT1, LMGT2
    Circuit Length: 5.793 km
    Laps Completed: 173
    Distance Covered: 1002.189 km
    Number of cars entered: 45 (14 LMP1, 15 LMP2, 4 LMGT1, 12 LMGT2)
    Number of cars finished: 28 (8 LMP1, 9 LMP2, 4 LMGT1, 7 LMGT2)
    Pole Position: #7 Team Peugeot Total, Peugeot 908 HDi FAP, Nicolas Minassian(FRA), Marc Gene(ESP), 1.31,470
    Overall Winner: #8 Team Peugeot Total, Peugeot 908 HDi FAP, Stephane Sarrazin(FRA), Pedro Lamy(POR), 4:59.07,955
    LMP2 Winner: #31 Team Essex, Porsche RS Spyder Evo, Casper Elgaard(DEN), John Nielsen(DEN), +8 Laps
    LMGT1 Winner: #59 Team Modena, Aston Martin DBR9, Tomas Enge(CZE), Antonio Garcia(ESP), +14 Laps
    LMGT2 Winner: #91 Farnbacher Racing, Porsche 997 GT3-RSR, Richard Westbrook(GBR), Allan Simonsen(DEN), Lars-Erik Nielsen(DEN), +22 Laps
    Drama for Audi before the start with #2 losing fuel pressure and stopping on the way to the grid, starting from the pit lane after being recovered back to the pits. Peugeot locked out the front row and led the start ahead of #1 Audi, with the Peugeots pulling out an early lead. #1 Audi struggled with tyre temps in the opening stages and pitted during an early safety car, however after the restart contact sent the car into a sizeable accident, briefly getting airbourne. The car managed to get back to the pits, but the extensive damage dropped the car several laps down. The Peugeots made their first stop under the resulting safety car, with #2 Audi briefly taking the lead until it pitted near the end of the first hour. #7 Peugeot slowed on track in the 2nd hour, a broken driveshaft after its 2nd stop forcing the car into the garage. #16 Pescarolo was running 3rd until a brake failure saw the car crash out during the 4th hour, retiring from the race. As the race reached the 4h mark a suspension failure pitched #5 Courage into an enormous accident, barrel rolling across the track and almost wiping out #1 Audi, scattering debris all over the track. The resulting safety car saw #2 Audi cycle to the lead, and as the race restarted it fought hard to stay ahead of #8 Peugeot. In the intense fight the Peugeot overtook traffic under waved yellow, and subsequently was handed a stop/go penalty. However the Audi had a miscommunication, and with #8 diving into T1 the cars made contact, with the Audi suffering a puncture. That allowed #8 Peugeot to serve its penalty and rejoin and take the win, with disappointment for Audi as #2 finished 2nd and Pescarolo bringing #17 home in 3rd.

  7. 1000 km of Spa
    Circuit de Spa-Franchorchamps, Stavelot, Belgium
    Date: 11.05.2008
    Series: LMS
    Race Format: 1000 km or 6 Hours
    Classes: LMP1, LMP2, LMGT1, LMGT2
    Circuit Length: 7.004 km
    Laps Completed: 143
    Distance Covered: 1001.572 km
    Number of cars entered: 44 (13 LMP1, 14 LMP2, 5 LMGT1, 12 LMGT2)
    Number of cars finished: 30 (10 LMP1, 7 LMP2, 4 LMGT1, 9 LMGT2)
    Pole Position: #8 Team Peugeot Total, Peugeot 908 HDi FAP, Stephane Sarrazin(FRA), Pedro Lamy(POR), Alexander Wurz(AUT), 1.58,069
    Overall Winner: #7 Team Peugeot Total, Peugeot 908 HDi FAP, Nicolas Minassian(FRA), Marc Gene(ESP), Jacques Villeneuve(CAN), 5:17.48,566
    LMP2 Winner: #34 Van Merksteijn Motorsport, Porsche RS Spyder Evo, Jos Verstappen(NED), Peter van Merksteijn Sr.(NED), +5 Laps
    LMGT1 Winner: #72 Luc Alphand Adventures, Chevrolet Corvette C6.R, Luc Alphand(FRA), Guillaume Moreau(FRA), Patrice Goueslard(FRA), +13 Laps
    LMGT2 Winner: #96 Virgo Motorsport, Ferrari F430 GT, Robert Bell(GBR), Gianmaria Bruni(ITA), +17 Laps
    #8 Peugeot qualified on pole ahead of #1 Audi, with the other Peugeot and Audi filling the 2nd row. The race started with an extra formation lap under safety car after an accident for #46 on the formation lap, with #8 Peugeot leading the start. #1 Audi initially lost time and came under pressure from #7, but after a lock up from the Peugeot #1 started catching the leading #8. The two Peugeots stopped first at the end of the opening hour, but the order remained the same after the Audis pitted 2 laps later. #1 Audi and #7 Peugeot tangled while fighting for 2nd at the start of the 2nd hour, the Audi suffering a puncture and forced to make another stop, rejoining 3rd. The Peugeots made their 2nd stop later in the 2nd hour, but #8 refused to start and lost a place to #7 which cycled to the lead once #1 Audi made its stop under safety car shortly after. Drama at the start of the 3rd hour as #8 Peugeot and #1 Audi made contact in traffic whilst battling for 2nd, #8 crashing out and retiring on the spot with the Audi ending up in the garage with a puncture and broken suspension. #1 Audi rejoined and made another stop still under the resulting safety car, but ignoring the red light at the pit exit resulted in a 3min stop/go. After all that it was #7 Peugeot leading ahead of #2 Audi, with the Peugeot cruising home to take the win as #2 Audi was involved in a late incident in traffic, escaping unscathed to finish 2nd.

  8. Larry H. Miller Dealerships Utah Grand Prix
    Miller Motorsports Park, Grantsville, Utah
    Date: 18.05.2008
    Series: ALMS
    Race Format: 2 Hours 45 minutes
    Classes: P1, P2, GT1, GT2
    Circuit Length: 4.905 km
    Laps Completed: 96
    Distance Covered: 470.880 km
    Number of cars entered: 30 (3 P1, 9 P2, 2 GT1, 16 GT2)
    Number of cars finished: 20 (2 P1, 9 P2, 2 GT1, 7 GT2)
    Pole Position: #7 Penske Motorsports, Porsche RS Spyder Evo, Timo Bernhard(DEU), Romain Dumas(FRA), 1.31,050
    Overall Winner: #7 Penske Motorsports, Porsche RS Spyder Evo, Timo Bernhard(DEU), Romain Dumas(FRA), 2:45.34,653
    P1 Winner: #2 Audi Sport North America, Audi R10 TDI, Marco Werner(DEU), Lucas Luhr(DEU), +1 Lap
    GT1 Winner: #3 Corvette Racing, Chevrolet Corvette C6.R, Johnny O'Connell(USA), Jan Magnussen(DEN), +8 Laps
    GT2 Winner: #45 Flying Lizard Motorsports, Porsche 997 GT3-RSR, Jörg Bergmeister(DEU), Wolf Henzler(DEU), +9 Laps
    #7 Porsche qualified on pole ahead of #15 Acura, with the new #66 Acura starting last after changing tyres before the race. The Audis stormed to the front from 5th and 7th on the grid, joined by the #37 Intersport which went from 10th on the grid to the lead in the opening laps, with all three cars scrapping for position. #37 started to fade a little after the first few laps, losing the lead to #1 Audi, and bringing the Porsches and Acuras back in the mix, eventually spinning while fighting #7 for 3rd. The two Audis and made their first stop under an early safety car, with #6 Porsche also stopping after an off-road excursion. #7 Porsche cycled to the lead, but on the restart #15 Acura went for the lead, but #9 and #26 Acuras tangled behind them with #9 breaking the suspension and losing time in the garage. #7 Porsche made its first stop under the resulting safety car, leaving #15 Acura in the lead ahead of #66. The Audis were fighting back, #2 moving up to 2nd and pressuring the leading #15 Acura. The two remaining Acuras stretched the first stint as long as possible, with #15 stopping after 1h 10min, with #66 following it a lap later. That left #2 Audi in the lead ahead of #1, with #7 Porsche 3rd. Contact between #20 Dyson and #15 Acura caused damage to the latter as #2 Audi made its 2nd stop, stalling and losing time exiting the pits. #1 stopped a lap later, and when #7 Porsche pitted from the lead #1 was leading ahead of #7 and #2 Audi. Audi split the strategy in the last stint, with #1 stopping from the lead for a splash, leaving #7 in the lead and #2 2nd but fuel saving. #66 Acura was moving up the order, briefly taking the lead before making its 2nd stop. Drama for the Audis as #2 suffered a puncture and spun out of 2nd, eliminated from the fight for the win, and shortly after #1 collided in traffic and retired with broken suspension. That left #7 Porsche out front to take the win, ahead of sister #6 and #66 Acura.

  9. 76e 24 Heures du Mans
    Circuit de la Sarthe, Le Mans, France
    Date: 14-15.06.2008
    Series: Standalone Event
    Race Format: 24 Hours
    Classes: LMP1, LMP2, LMGT1, LMGT2
    Circuit Length: 13.629 km
    Laps Completed: 381
    Distance Covered: 5192.649 km
    Number of cars entered: 55 (22 LMP1, 11 LMP2, 10 LMGT1, 12 LMGT2)
    Number of cars finished: 33 (13 LMP1, 6 LMP2, 8 LMGT1, 6 LMGT2)
    Pole Position: #8 Team Peugeot Total, Peugeot 908 HDi FAP, Stephane Sarrazin(FRA), Pedro Lamy(POR), Alexander Wurz(AUT), 3.18,513
    Overall Winner: #2 Audi Sport North America, Audi R10 TDI, Rinaldo Capello(ITA), Allan McNish(GBR), Tom Kristensen(DEN), 24:00.24,085
    LMP2 Winner: #34 Van Merksteijn Motorsport, Porsche RS Spyder Evo, Jos Verstappen(NED), Jeroen Bleekemolen(NED), Peter van Merksteijn Sr.(NED), +27 Laps
    LMGT1 Winner: #009 Aston Martin Racing, Aston Martin DBR9, David Brabham(AUS), Antonio Garcia(ESP), Darren Turner(GBR), +37 Laps
    LMGT2 Winner: #82 Risi Competizione, Ferrari F430 GT, Mika Salo(FIN), Jaime Melo(BRA), Gianmaria Bruni(ITA), +55 Laps
    The trio of Peugeots qualified in front and controlled the start with the Audis following in 4th, 5th and 7th, with #2 Audi briefly taking 3rd from #7 on the opening lap. The Peugeots started to pull away, with #8 leading until a gearbox issue forced it into the garage in the 3rd hour. At the same time #9 was also forced to make an extra stop to change the nose after a headlight failed. That left #2 Audi in the lead, having made fewer pit stops and spent less time in the pits. However Peugeot fought back, and #7 took the lead as the race reached 4 hours with #2 demoted to 3rd by #9 late in the 5th hour. #9 then took the lead from #7 in the 6th hour, but an hour later it went off and got stuck in the gravel. Forced to be rescued out it handed the lead to #7 and #2 went into 2nd. Going into the 10th hour #8 suffered more issues, going back in the garage with starter motor issues. Drama as all three Peugeots visited the garage in the 13th hour, all three getting temperature warnings and stopping to clear the radiators. #2 Audi briefly took the lead as the problems unfolded for Peugeot, but #7 quickly cycled back to the lead as #2 made its next scheduled stop. Rain started falling early in the 14th hour, with #8 and #9 initially pitting for inters. as the rain intensified the rest of the leaders pitted for wets, with #8 and #9 forced to pit again for wets. The extra stop for #9 Peugeot gifted 3rd place to #3 Audi. The rain handed the advantage to Audi, with #2 moving into the lead in the 15th hour. #9 Peugeot moved back past #3 into 3rd as the race moved into its 16th hour, where #16 Pescarolo retired with engine failure. Peugeot started experimenting with downforce setup on #8, and as the track started drying in the 19th hour #7 pitted for a new rear with a different downforce level. The track continued to dry, and in the 20th hour #3 and #1 Audi pitted for inters. however #1 struggled, spinning and then slowing, limping back to the garage with clutch issues. The rest of the leaders gradually switched to inters over the course of the next hour, before #1 Audi switched to slicks. The rest followed, but #8 went back into the garage for a brief stop to clear the radiators. #3 Audi was in at the same time, it too having its radiators cleared. Shortly after #8 went off and hit the wall, after being pulled out it returned to the pits for replacement bodywork. Rain started falling again with just over 1 hour to go, with #2 stopping for inters. #7 meanwhile stuck to slicks, with heavy rain on half the track and the rest dry. #1 Audi spun out in the final hour, getting stuck in the gravel and having to be pulled out. #7 pitted again to try wets, but a loose wheel forced it go come back in, losing any hope of the win. #2 Audi made its last stop with 13 minutes to go, and duly cruised home to take a famous win with Peugeot bringing home #7 and #9 to complete the podium.

Season Totals:

Number of Races: 17
Total Distance Covered: 17699.754 km



2009 Season

Overview:

Following record-breaking speed in 2008 the ACO adjusted the technical regulations for LMP1 and LMP2 to slow the cars down and continue to equalize the performance between diesel and petrol-powered cars. IMSA finally implemented the full ACO regulations to differentiate LMP1 and LMP2, having deliberately kept the classes closer the 2 previous years.
After competing on all fronts in 2008, and following the impact of the global economic crisis, for 2009 Audi scaled back to just competing in selected events, predominantly the major endurance events in Sebring, Le Mans and Petit Le Mans. Team Joest took over the whole operation, leaving Champion Racing behind. They also brought in a new car in the form of the R15 to replace the outgoing R10.
Peugeot also scaled back their involvement, going into their third year with the 908. In late 2008 they also revealed a modified hybrid version of the car called the 908 HY, but they never planned to race it.
After 3 years of success in the ALMS Porsche ended the factory program, leaving the RS Spyder in hands of privateers.
Acura continued its project in the US, after running for 2 years in LMP2 with the ARX-01, for 2009 they debuted the ARX-02 in the LMP1 class. Highcroft Racing and de Ferran Motorsports took on the new car, with Fernandez Racing continuing in LMP2 with the ARX-01 in LMP2.
Pescarolo went into its 3rd season with an updated 01 Evo, but financial strain saw the company sold. The team continued operating as Pescarolo Sport in LMS with 1 full season entry and 1 only for the first half, and for Le Mans they brought a customer Peugeot alongside one of their own chassis. The team also competed in the AsLMS, but due to the new ownership the team was entered as SORA Racing.
Having taken over Courage in 2007, Oreca developed a new car for 2009 in the form of the 01. The team staterd the season with the old Courages, before debuting the new car at Spa and competing at Le Mans and the rest of the LMS.
Economic concerns and regulation changes saw Creation start winding down operations. The team chose to only bring a single car to Le Mans, while focusing on supporting its customers.
Epsilon Euskadi also withdrew from sportscars in 2009, with the team focusing on its single seater program and planning an entry to F1.
Lavaggi was also forced to update the car for 2009, but the economic difficulties meant the updates couldn't be tested in the wind tunnel, meaning the car became very difficult to drive. The team aimed to continue competing in the LMS, but economic difficulties meant the team shut down by the end of the season.
A newcomer to the top class for 2009 was Aston Martin, debuting the AMR1-2 and taking on a full LMS season.
Meanwhile in the GT categories, BMW returned with a factory team in the GT2 class for the first time since 2001, partnering with team RLL. After racing alone in GT1 for several years Corvette Racing took the desicion to modify their car to GT2-spec. They started in GT1 for the first few races whilst the new car was developed, but moved to GT2 for the 2nd half of the season.
ALMS continued to target stabilisation, keeping all the events from 2008, the only change being Road America going back to the standard 2h 45min format. With the number of entries reduced following Audi's withdrawal as a full time entrant IMSA allowed teams from the Porsche cup challenge to race at selected events in their own class.
The LMS made a few changes for their 2009 calendar, with Monza being replaced by a night event at the new Algarve circuit in Portugal.
After the planned AsLMS race in Shanghai was cancelled in 2008, plans for a series launch in 2009 were still on, with 2 events in Okayama in Japan and Shanghai in China, and a revised format with 2 500km races per event.

Calendar:

  1. 57th Annual Mobil 1 12 Hours of Sebring
    Sebring International Raceway, Sebring, Florida
    Date: 21.03.2009
    Series: ALMS
    Race Format: 12 Hours
    Classes: P1, P2, GT1, GT2
    Circuit Length: 6.019 km
    Laps Completed: 383
    Distance Covered: 2305.277 km
    Number of cars entered: 27 (8 P1, 3 P2, 2 GT1, 14 GT2)
    Number of cars finished: 14 (3 P1, 1 P2, 2 GT1, 8 GT2)
    Pole Position: #66 de Ferran Motorsport, Acura ARX-02a, Gil de Ferran(BRA), Simon Pagenaud(FRA), Scott Dixon(NZE), 1.45,278
    Overall Winner: #2 Audi Sport Team Joest, Audi R15 TDI, Rinaldo Capello(ITA), Allan McNish(GBR), Tom Kristensen(DEN), 12:00.38,638
    P2 Winner: #15 Lowe's Fernandez Racing, Acura ARX-01b, Adrian Fernandez(MEX), Luis Diaz(MEX), +23 Laps
    GT1 Winner: #3 Corvette Racing, Chevrolet Corvette C6.R, Johnny O'Connell(USA), Jan Magnussen(DEN), Antonio Garcia(ESP), +34 Laps
    GT2 Winner: #62 Risi Competizione, Ferrari F430 GT, Mika Salo(FIN), Jaime Melo(BRA), Pierre Kaffer(DEU), +51 Laps
    #66 Acura qualified on pole ahead of #2 Audi and #07 Peugeot, as #08 Peugeot was forced to start from the back after a hydraulic failure in the warm-up. #2 Audi immediately took the lead at the start with #07 Peugeot also taking 2nd from #66 on the first lap with #66 shuffled back to 4th. As the leaders made their first stop #07 Peugeot took the lead after taking fuel only, however #2 Audi fought back to take the lead on fresher tyres early in the 2nd hour with #07 dropping back throughout the stint and eventually losing 2nd to #1. #9 Acura spun off later in the 2nd hour, bringing out the safety car. #07 Peugeot made its 2nd stop just before the safety car came out, cycling to the lead when the rest of the leaders made their stop when the pits opened, with #08 Peugeot also moving into 3rd ahead of #1 Audi. #1 Audi then tangled in traffic and spun, while #08 Peugeot caught and passed #2 Audi for 2nd into the 3rd hour. As the leaders made their 3rd stop Peugeot again took fuel only and extended the gap to the Audis. Another safety car later in the 3rd hour saw the leaders stop again, with the Audis taking time to remove debris from the radiators and replace the engine covers. Drama in the 4th hour as #07 Peugeot spun off, handing the lead to #08 and dropping to 4th behind both Audis. More pit cycles saw #07 back in 2nd until #2 Audi caught and passed it into the 5th hour, as moments later #08 spun and only just held on to the lead. Later in the 5th hour #07 Peugeot pitted with electrical issues caused by a malfunctioning air condition, dropping several laps down. #2 Audi was gradually catching the leading #08, and as they cycled through the pits 5h in the Audi took the lead. However the Peugeot stayed within reach, and at the next stop an hour later it took fuel only and emerged back in the lead. Shortly after #66 Acura pitted with smoke from the car, but after a quick check rejoined. Sister #9 spun out in the 7th hour, and struggling to start the car meant the safety car was deployed. The leaders pitted with #08 maintaining the lead, as the Acura pitted for repairs. As the leaders pitted in the 8th hour #1 Audi took fuel only, trying a double stint for the first time. That allowed it to briefly take 2nd behind #08 Peugeot. Problems struck #66 Acura at the 8h mark, going to the garage and retiring with suspension issues and a fuel leak. Into the 9th hour and #9 also hit problems, struggling with the hydraulic power steering. At the same time #2 Audi was pressuring #08 Peugeot, and the Audi briefly took the lead before pitting. The Peugeot stopped a lap later, with the Audi maintaining the lead. Approaching 9h #08 Peugeot pitted out of sequence with a slow puncture. When #2 Audi pitted from the lead early in the 10th hour the Peugeot cycled to the lead until it made its next scheduled stop. #9 Acura continued to struggle with the power steering, and in the 11th hour the car went to the garage and retired with gearbox failure. #07 Peugeot stopped on track and retired with gearbox failure in the final hour, as #2 Audi controlled the closing stages to take the win despite a late splash with #08 Peugeot finishing 2nd ahead of #1.

  2. Acura Sports Car Challenge of St. Petersburg
    Streets of St. Petersburg, St. Petersburg, Florida
    Date: 04.04.2009
    Series: ALMS
    Race Format: 1 Hour 55 minutes
    Classes: P1, P2, GT2
    Circuit Length: 2.910 km
    Laps Completed: 93
    Distance Covered: 270.630 km
    Number of cars entered: 17 (3 P1, 3 P2, 11 GT2)
    Number of cars finished: 12 (2 P1, 3 P2, 7 GT2)
    Pole Position: #66 de Ferran Motorsport, Acura ARX-02a, Gil de Ferran(BRA), Simon Pagenaud(FRA), 1.03,776
    Overall Winner: #9 Patron Highcroft Racing, Acura ARX-02a, Scott Sharp(USA), David Brabham(AUS), 1:55.53,705
    P2 Winner: #15 Lowe's Fernandez Racing, Acura ARX-01b, Adrian Fernandez(MEX), Luis Diaz(MEX), +32,150
    GT2 Winner: #45 Flying Lizard Motorsports, Porsche 997 GT3-RSR, Jörg Bergmeister(DEU), Patrick Long(USA), +5 Laps
    #66 Acura qualified on pole ahead of #9 and #15, and controlled the opening stages as #9 lost time with a brief spin that dropped it behind #15. #66 made its first stop 50 min in, but a safety car just afterwards saw #9 and #15 make their first stop and rejoin ahead with #15 resuming the lead. #66 started suffering technical problems and pitted as #9 took the lead after pressuring #15. #66 Acura continued to suffer electrical issues, with the team unable to diagnose it, and eventually stopped on track and retired. Meanwhile #9 Acura cruised home to take the win, with #15 Acura finishing 2nd.

  3. 1000 km de Catalunya
    Circuit de Catalunya, Montmelo, Spain
    Date: 05.04.2009
    Series: LMS
    Race Format: 1000 km or 6 Hours
    Classes: LMP1, LMP2, LMGT1, LMGT2
    Circuit Length: 4.655 km
    Laps Completed: 209
    Distance Covered: 972.895 km
    Number of cars entered: 43 (11 LMP1, 15 LMP2, 4 LMGT1, 13 LMGT2)
    Number of cars finished: 30 (8 LMP1, 9 LMP2, 3 LMGT1, 10 LMGT2)
    Pole Position: #23 Strakka Racing, Ginetta-Zytek GZ09S, Peter Hardman(GBR), Danny Watts(GBR), Nick Leventis(GBR), 1.32,492
    Overall Winner: #007 Aston Martin Racing, Lola Aston Martin DBR1-2, Jan Charouz(CZE), Tomas Enge(CZE), Stefan Mücke(DEU), 6:00.05,674
    LMP2 Winner: #30 Racing Box, Lola B08/80 - Judd, Andrea Piccini(ITA), Matteo Bobbi(ITA), Thomas Biagi(ITA), +8 Laps
    LMGT1 Winner: #55 IPB Spartak Racing, Lamborghini Murcielago R-GT, Peter Kox(NED), Roman Rusinov(RUS), +20 Laps
    LMGT2 Winner: #77 Team Felbermayr-Proton, Porsche 997 GT3-RSR, Marc Lieb(DEU), Richard Lietz(AUT), +22 Laps
    #23 Strakka qualified on pole ahead of the two Astons, however #007 went from 3rd to the lead immediately, followed by #13 Lola and #009. An early safety car saw the leaders make their first stop, but chaos in the pit lane saw #16 Pescarolo take the lead ahead of #009 and #13. Another safety car in the 2nd hour saw the leaders make their 2nd stop, except #13 which cycled to the lead ahead of #007. As the race restarted #16 Pescarolo put pressure on #009 and took 3rd. #13 eventually made its 2nd stop, handing the lead to #007 Aston. As the leaders made their 3rd stop #16 Pescarolo took the lead with #007 Aston taking full service. #007 pressured #16 throughout the stint, but as they were stuck in traffic it allowed #11 Oreca to catch them, and into the 4th hour it took 2nd from the Aston. However soon after it pitted with gearbox issues. #16 maintained the lead through the next pit cycle, and a spin from #007 towards the end of the 4th hour gave the Pescarolo a comfortable lead. #16 made its final stop early in the final hour and maintained the lead, but shortly after #009 Aston spun and retired with gearbox failure, bringing out the safety car. As the race restarted #007 closed down the leading Pescarolo, and as #16 got baulked in traffic the Aston took the lead and cruised home to take the win, with #16 Pescarolo coming home 2nd.

  4. American Le Mans Series at Long Beach
    Long Beach Street Circuit, Long Beach, California
    Date: 18.04.2009
    Series: ALMS
    Race Format: 1 Hour 40 minutes
    Classes: P1, P2, GT1, GT2
    Circuit Length: 3.167 km
    Laps Completed: 76
    Distance Covered: 240.692 km
    Number of cars entered: 21 (4 P1, 3 P2, 2 GT1, 12 GT2)
    Number of cars finished: 18 (4 P1, 3 P2, 1 GT1, 10 GT2)
    Pole Position: #9 Patron Highcroft Racing, Acura ARX-02a, Scott Sharp(USA), David Brabham(AUS), 1.11,627
    Overall Winner: #66 de Ferran Motorsport, Acura ARX-02a, Gil de Ferran(BRA), Simon Pagenaud(FRA), 1:41.42,927
    P2 Winner: #15 Lowe's Fernandez Racing, Acura ARX-01b, Adrian Fernandez(MEX), Luis Diaz(MEX), +1 Lap
    GT1 Winner: #4 Corvette Racing, Chevrolet Corvette C6.R, Oliver Gavin(GBR), Olivier Beretta(MCO), +3 Laps
    GT2 Winner: #45 Flying Lizard Motorsports, Porsche 997 GT3-RSR, Jörg Bergmeister(DEU), Patrick Long(USA), +5 Laps
    #9 Acura qualified on pole ahead of #66 and #15, but #66 took the lead at the start 2nd time around after the first start was waved off as the cars were not lined up properly. #9 fought back to re-take the lead later in the first stint, as #9 and #15 Acuras pitted together after 1 hour, however #9 was penalized 20s for a pit stop infringement that later turned out to be incorrect. #66 Acura stopped from the lead a few laps later and rejoined in the lead, controlling the closing stages to take the win. After the debacle in the pits #9 Acura fought back to take 2nd from #15 as they manouvered through #25 and #90 tangling, with the race ending under safety car after a fire for #25.

  5. 1000 km of Spa
    Circuit de Spa-Franchorchamps, Stavelot, Belgium
    Date: 10.05.2009
    Series: LMS
    Race Format: 1000 km or 6 Hours
    Classes: LMP1, LMP2, LMGT1, LMGT2
    Circuit Length: 7.004 km
    Laps Completed: 143
    Distance Covered: 1001.572 km
    Number of cars entered: 51 (15 LMP1, 17 LMP2, 3 LMGT1, 16 LMGT2)
    Number of cars finished: 33 (12 LMP1, 7 LMP2, 3 LMGT1, 11 LMGT2)
    Pole Position: #7 Team Peugeot Total, Peugeot 908 HDi FAP, Nicolas Minassian(FRA), Simon Pagenaud(FRA), Christian Klien(AUT), 2.01,056
    Overall Winner: #7 Team Peugeot Total, Peugeot 908 HDi FAP, Nicolas Minassian(FRA), Simon Pagenaud(FRA), Christian Klien(AUT), 5:45.35,429
    LMP2 Winner: #31 Team Essex, Porsche RS Spyder Evo, Casper Elgaard(DEN), Kristian Poulsen(DEN), Emmanuel Collard(FRA), +4 Laps
    LMGT1 Winner: #72 Luc Alphand Adventures, Chevrolet Corvette C6.R, Luc Alphand(FRA), Yann Clairay(FRA), Patrice Goueslard(FRA), +11 Laps
    LMGT2 Winner: #77 Team Felbermayr-Proton, Porsche 997 GT3-RSR, Marc Lieb(DEU), Richard Lietz(AUT), Horst Felbermayr Sr(AUT), +14 Laps
    Peugeot locked out the front row ahead of #009 Aston, as sister #007 started from the pit lane after problems in qualifying. #7 Peugeot controlled the start as several cars stranded on the formation lap and contact between #009 Aston and #16 Pescarolo brought out the safety car, with #009 limping back with a puncture and #16 spinning. Another safety car in the opening hour saw #17 Pescarolo tangle on the restart, pitting with suspension issues. The early safety cars allowed #009 Aston to recover, and by the end of the first hour the car was back in 3rd as the leaders made their first stop. #7 maintained the lead, but #16 Pescarolo was putting heavy pressure on until it made its first stop a few laps later. The Peugeots maintained the lead through the 2nd pit cycle, but early in the 3rd hour #9 pitted and went into the garage with suspension issues and dropped several laps down. Later in the same hour #17 Pescarolo suffered a big accident, spreading debris all over the track and bringing out the safety car. Both Astons were forced to pit with non-functioning headlights, allowing #11 Oreca into 2nd ahead of #16 Pescarolo, with #7 Peugeot still leading. As the race entered the 5th hour #16 Pescarolo was catching #11, which first collided with the #15 Kolles Audi, and then tangled in traffic, allowing the Pescarolo to take 2nd. Meanwhile #7 Peugeot controlled the closing stages to take the win ahead of #16 Pescarolo, ahead of #007 Aston which took 3rd after a late scrap with #11.

    Pole Position: #66 de Ferran Motorsport, Acura ARX-02a, Gil de Ferran(BRA), Simon Pagenaud(FRA), 1.30,645
    Overall Winner: #66 de Ferran Motorsport, Acura ARX-02a, Gil de Ferran(BRA), Simon Pagenaud(FRA), 2:46.14,913

  7. 77e 24 Heures du Mans
    Circuit de la Sarthe, Le Mans, France
    Date: 13-14.06.2009
    Series: Standalone Event
    Race Format: 24 Hours
    Classes: LMP1, LMP2, LMGT1, LMGT2
    Circuit Length: 13.629 km
    Laps Completed: 382
    Distance Covered: 5206.278 km
    Number of cars entered: 55 (20 LMP1, 12 LMP2, 6 LMGT1, 17 LMGT2)
    Number of cars finished: 32 (15 LMP1, 4 LMP2, 3 LMGT1, 10 LMGT2)
    Pole Position: #8 Team Peugeot Total, Peugeot 908 HDi FAP, Stephane Sarrazin(FRA), Franck Montagny(FRA), Sebastien Bourdais(FRA), 3.22,888
    Overall Winner: #9 Peugeot Sport Total, Peugeot 908 HDi FAP, David Brabham(AUS), Marc Gene(ESP), Alexander Wurz(AUT), 24:01.45,442
    LMP2 Winner: #31 Team Essex, Porsche RS Spyder Evo, Casper Elgaard(DEN), Kristian Poulsen(DEN), Emmanuel Collard(FRA), +25 Laps
    LMGT1 Winner: #63 Corvette Racing, Chevrolet Corvette C6.R, Johnny O'Connell(USA), Jan Magnussen(DEN), Antonio Garcia(ESP), +40 Laps
    LMGT2 Winner: #82 Risi Competizione, Ferrari F430 GT, Mika Salo(FIN), Jaime Melo(BRA), Pierre Kaffer(DEU), +53 Laps
    #8 Peugeot qualified on pole ahead of #1 Audi, with #7 and #17 Pescarolo Peugeot on the 2nd row. #8 controlled the start as #7 and #9 moved up to lie 2nd and 3rd in the opening laps, demoting #1 Audi to 4th. #3 Audi went off just a few minutes into the race, getting stuck in the gravel and returning to the pits with front end damage. As the leaders made their first stop there was drama in the pits as #7 Peugeot and #17 collided, #17 suffering nose damage and spent time in the garage, while #7 suffered a puncture which caused extensive damage limping back to the pits, dropping 7 laps down. The resulting safety car saw the Audis make their first stop as #009 Aston went into the garage with a broken alternator belt. The safety car allowed #9 Peugeot to make an extra stop to top up the fuel, with #8 Peugeot leading from #1 Audi and #007 Aston. As the race restarted #2 Audi took 3rd from the Aston, and as the leaders made their 2nd stop #2 Audi took 2nd as #1 dropped behind #9 to 4th after a nose change. #9 Peugeot then pressured #2 Audi and moved into 2nd as the race reached 2 hours, with #1 Audi moving into 3rd at the 3rd pit cycle. As the race reached 4 hours #009 Aston was back in the garage with electrical issues as the Audis kept swapping positions through the pit cycles, with #2 taking a new nose to try to find more pace. Into the 5th hour and #009 hit problems again, colliding with #26 which crashed out. The accident saw another safety car period, and the driver in the Aston was excluded from the rest of the race. As the race restarted #3 Audi returned to the garage with engine issues. Drama late in the 6th hour as #8 Peugeot pitted from the lead and went into the garage with gearbox issues, #9 took over the lead followed by #1 and #2 Audis as #8 rejoined 4th. The drama continued in the 7th hour as #2 Audi crashed out after suffering a suspension failure. That left #1 in 3rd ahead of the recovering #8 Peugeot which was in a fight with #17 and #008 Aston. #008 Aston pitted in the 8th hour and went into the garage with a broken wheel and suspension damage after contact. Towards the end of the hour #1 Audi pitted and went into the garage briefly to clear the radiators, dropping behind #8 Peugeot to 3rd. However as the race entered its 9th hour #8 was involved in an incident and required a new nose at its next stop, dropping back behind the Audi. #1 Audi had another visit to the garage as the race passed the half way point, clearing out the brake ducts before rejoining behind #8 Peugeot. Shortly after #7 has another visit to the garage with suspension issues. Drama as the race reached 13 hours as #17 Pescarolo Peugeot suffered a big accident, the car destroyed after crashing out from 4th. #1 Audi took the opportunity to visit the garage again under the resulting safety car to clear the radiators. The accident for #17 left #007 Aston in 4th overall. As dawn broke and the race went into the 17th hour #008 Aston suffered more issues, going into the garage with gearbox issues and dropping out of the top 10. The car briefly rejoined in the 18th hour but a suspension failure sent the car back to the garage. #16 Pescarolo had a steady race until a visit to the garage around the same time. Into the 19th hour and #1 had another trip to the garage to clear radiators before rejoining, still 3rd but dropping further behind the Peugeots ahead. Later in the same hour #009 Aston crashed out and retired to end a miserable, trouble-filled race. After the safety car period #3 Audi went off and got stuck in the gravel, before limping back to the garage. Electrical issues struck #1 Audi in the 21st hour along with suspension issues and sent it back to the garage, this time a longer stop allowing #007 Aston to close the gap. #9 Peugeot cruised home to take the win with sister #8 following it home ahead of #1 Audi after a difficult race.

Season Totals:

Number of Races: 18
Total Distance Covered: 17659.220 km



2010 Season

Overview:

After a disappointing 2009 season Audi launched 2010 with a heavily revised R15 TDI Plus, debuting the car at the LMS Opener at Castellet before bringing it to Spa before Le Mans.
Peugeot ran a similar program to 2009 with more minor updated to the 908 HDi FAP, competing at Sebring and Spa in preparation for Le Mans.
After winning the Le Mans Series in 2009 Aston Martin went into their 2nd season targeting a variety of events, bringing a car to Sebring, Le Castellet and Long Beach before Le Mans, and then competing at selected races afterwards.
Oreca continued into 2010 racing selected events with the 01, but their main focus was their customer Peugeot.
Acura withdrew from the ALMS for 2010, but HPD continued the program and continued their partnership with Highcroft as well as forming a new partnership with Strakka Racing in Europe. The ARX-02 was abandoned with the team racing a single updated ARX-01c in the ALMS, and for the first time bringing the car to Le Mans. Fernandez Racing and de Ferran Motorsport both closed their doors following the 2009 season.
After selling the team in 2009, the economic difficulties continued for Pescarolo, and going into 2010 the team was shut down and the team went into administration later in the year.
ALMS revealed a new class structure for 2010, with LMP1 and LMP2 cars compined into a single class for all rounds except Sebring and Petit Le Mans. A new class was added in the form of Prototype Challenge, using the new Oreca FLM chassis based on the Courage LC75. After competing at 5 rounds in 2009 the Challenge class became GTC and joined the series full-time in 2010, opening up to include other versions of the Porsche cup-car.
LMS also revised its class structure, it too adding a fifth class for the Oreca FLM which came from a project between Oreca and the ACO.
ALMS revealed a slightly revised calendar for 2010, with St. Petersburg dropping off the calendar, and Laguna Seca moving to May and being extended to 6 Hours.
The LMS also revealed a slightly modified calendar, with Catalunya and Nurburgring being replaced by Paul Ricard and Hungaroring, and the former being 8 Hours instead of the usual 1000km/6 hours.
Also announced in 2010 was the Intercontinental Le Mans Cup, a new championship taking in 3 races across the 3 Le Mans Series', starting at the LMS race at Silverstone before moving to the Petit Le Mans and ending at the sole AsLMS race at Zhuhai. Peugeot joined, as did Audi, both with 2 cars each.

  1. 58th Annual Mobil 1 12 Hours of Sebring
    Sebring International Raceway, Sebring, Florida
    Date: 20.03.2010
    Series: ALMS
    Race Format: 12 Hours
    Classes: P1, P2, PC, GT2, GTC
    Circuit Length: 6.019 km
    Laps Completed: 367
    Distance Covered: 2208.973 km
    Number of cars entered: 35 (6 P1, 3 P2, 6 PC, 13 GT2, 7 GTC)
    Number of cars finished: 26 (4 P1, 3 P2, 2 PC, 10 GT2, 7 GTC)
    Pole Position: #07 Team Peugeot Total, Peugeot 908 HDi FAP, Marc Gene(ESP), Alexander Wurz(AUT), Anthony Davidson(GBR), 1.45,214
    Overall Winner: #07 Team Peugeot Total, Peugeot 908 HDi FAP, Marc Gene(ESP), Alexander Wurz(AUT), Anthony Davidson(GBR), 12:00.54,362
    P2 Winner: #6 Muscle Milk Team Cytosport, Porsche RS Spyder Evo, Sascha Maassen(DEU), Klaus Graf(DEU), Greg Pickett(USA), +14 Laps
    GT2 Winner: #62 Risi Competizione, Ferrari F430 GT, Gianmaria Bruni(ITA), Jaime Melo(BRA), Pierre Kaffer(DEU), +36 Laps
    PC Winner: #55 Level 5 Motorsports, Oreca FLM09 - Chevrolet, Christophe Bouchut(FRA), Mark Wilkins(CAN), Scott Tucker(USA), +40 Laps
    GTC Winner: #81 Alex Job Racing, Porsche 997 GT3 Cup, Butch Leitzinger(USA), Leh Keen(USA), Juan Gonzalez(MEX), +59 Laps
    Peugeot locked out the front row ahead of #007 Aston, but a good start saw #8 Drayson take 3rd from #007, and after pressuring #08 in traffic #8 took 2nd. The leaders made their first stop at the end of the first hour, with #08 taking fuel only and rejoining in the lead, with #8 dropping to 3rd after its stop before taking 2nd from #07 which struggled on cold tyres. A safety car shortly after saw #007 Aston make an additional stop for a splash, as #8 made its 2nd stop half way through the 2nd hour. The leading Peugeots made their 2nd stop near the end of the 2nd hour with #08 maintaining the lead as #8 pressured from behind. #8 then suffered alternator issues in the 3rd hour, a lengthy visit in the pits costing it time and handed 3rd to #007. #08 Peugeot controlled the lead for the next few hours, with #07 trying to keep up, but a spin in the 5th hour cost it time. A safety car in the 7th hour saw the leaders stop together, but #08 then pitted out of sequence at the end of the hour and handed the lead to #07. Another safety car in the 8th hour saw the leaders again stop together, with #08 rejoining back in the lead. However as they pitted early in the 9th hour it was #07 emerging in the lead. #07 then controlled the remaining hours, made its last stop 45 min from the end and cruised home to take the win, with sister #08 making its last stop 5 min later on course to finish 2nd. #007 Aston finished a lonely 3rd, 3 laps down.

However the Audi quickly fought back to take the lead, with #4 following it into 2nd. #009 then suffered a puncture later in the opening stint, costing it time and forcing it off sequence with the others. The leaders made their first stop at the end of the opening hour, but #4 suffered a proplem with the pneumatic jacks and was forced into the garage and dropped 8 laps. That left #7 Audi in the lead ahead of #009 Aston and #13 Rebellion. #7 controlled the race from the front, and as the race entered the final hour #009 made its final stop from 2nd, but a long stop cost it time and saw #13 close the gap. Rain started falling in the final 10 min, and #7 Audi stopped for wets before cruising home to take the win ahead of #009 Aston and #13 Rebellion. #4 Oreca Peugeot recovered from its early drama to finish 4th.

After a series of early safety cars #37 made a blinding restart to take the lead, and as #007 and #1 scrapped for 2nd they collided, sending #007 into the wall and damaging the rear, and #1 was handed a stop/go for the incident. However #1 fought back and barged its way back into the lead on the final lap as #007 struggled with the brakes to take the win.

  4. 1000 km de Spa-Franchorchamps
    Circuit de Spa-Franchorchamps, Stavelot, Belgium
    Date: 09.05.2010
    Series: LMS
    Race Format: 1000 km or 6 Hours
    Classes: LMP1, LMP2, FLM, LMGT1, LMGT2
    Circuit Length: 7.004 km
    Laps Completed: 139
    Distance Covered: 973.556 km
    Number of cars entered: 50 (10 LMP1, 11 LMP2, 6 FLM, 7 LMGT1, 16 LMGT2)
    Number of cars finished: 39 (8 LMP1, 7 LMP2, 3 FLM, 6 LMGT1, 15 LMGT2)
    Pole Position: #3 Team Peugeot Total, Peugeot 908 HDi FAP, Pedro Lamy(POR), Sebastien Bourdais(FRA), Simon Pagenaud(FRA), 1.57,884
    Overall Winner: #3 Team Peugeot Total, Peugeot 908 HDi FAP, Pedro Lamy(POR), Sebastien Bourdais(FRA), Simon Pagenaud(FRA), 6:00.39,012
    LMP2 Winner: #40 Quifel ASM Team, Ginetta-Zytek GZ09SB/2, Miguel Amaral(POR), Olivier Pla(FRA), +9 Laps
    FLM Winner: #47 Hope Polevision Racing, Oreca FLM09 - Chevrolet, Steve Zacchia(CHE), Luca Moro(ITA), Wolfgang Kaufmann(DEU), +15 Laps
    LMGT2 Winner: #77 Team Felbermayr-Proton, Porsche 997 GT3-RSR, Marc Lieb(DEU), Richard Lietz(AUT), +15 Laps
    LMGT1 Winner: #70 Marc VDS Racing Team, Ford GT1, Eric De Doncker(BEL), Bas Leinders(BEL), Markus Palttala(FIN), +16 Laps
    #3 Peugeot qualified on pole ahead of #9 Audi, with #2 and #4 Oreca Peugeot filling the 2nd row. Drama before the start as #8 Audi went off on the formation lap in damp conditions, bringing the car back to the pits for repairs. #4 also spun but managed to rejoin and took the start as normal. At the start #3 Peugeot spun, handing the lead to #2 ahead of #4 as #7 and #9 Audis were shuffled back. However #1 then took 2nd ahead of #7 as #4 dropped back by the time an early safety car came out. As the race restarted #4 collided with #13 Rebellion, sending #4 off and into retirement. #13 then continued moving up the order, taking 3rd from #7. Meanwhile #3 was fighting back, taking 5th from #12 Rebellion before #7 Audi took 3rd from #13 with #3 following through. #3 then put pressure on the Audi and took 3rd. As the track was drying #3 started closing the gap with #2 still leading ahead of #1. Another safety car towards the end of the opening hour saw #7 make its first stop, with the rest of the leaders staying out. #7 rejoined 5th but quickly took 4th from #9 as the race restarted, and cycled to the lead as the rest of the leaders made their first stop. Drama as a power outage struck the whole circuit towards the end of the 2nd hour, with the backup power system kicking in but timing and scoring went blank and the TV broadcast ceased. As the leaders made their 2nd stop at the end of the 2nd hour #7 stayed ahead of #3 Peugeot as #2 tangled in traffic and went off, limping back to the pits with substantial damage. #1 cycled to the lead having not stopped before the race was red flagged around the 2h mark as the backup power was running out and race control was set to lose CCTV and the ability to communicate with the marshals. As the race restarted later in the 3rd hour #1 pitted and handed the lead to #7 Audi, which now faced intense pressure from #3 Peugeot. The pair traded places into the 4th hour, but the Audi stayed ahead. The leaders made their 3rd stop with #3 taking fuel only and rejoining in the lead, with #7 struggling throughout the stint. The Audi continued to struggle after another cycle through the pits, dropping back towards #1 and eventually losing 2nd as #3 continued to lead. Another safety car as the final hour started, #1 made its final stop followed by #2, with #3 and #7 staying out. Rain started falling in the final hour, and #3 made its final stop 30 min from the end and took inters as #7 and #1 struggled on slicks with #1 going off. #7 stopped for inters and started catching #3 which then went grass-trekking, but as the track started drying again #3 got back to speed and cruised home to the win, with #7 starting to struggle and lost 2nd to #2 in the final minutes.

    Overall Winner: #1 Patron Highcroft Racing, HPD ARX-01c, David Brabham(AUS), Simon Pagenaud(FRA), Marino Franchitti(GBR), 6:00.09,654

A blinding start saw #37 Intersport go from 3rd to the lead at the start, with #1 moving through the field to take 4th in the opening stages. After an early safety car #16, #6 and #1 all scrapped for 2nd, with #6 taking 2nd from #16, and #1 demoting the Dyson to 4th. Drama as #37 suffered a turbo failure towards the end of the first hour, and pitted to retire. That left #6 in the lead, as #16 made its first stop early in the 2nd hour, but was handed a stop/go for speeding in the pit lane. #1 made its first stop a few laps later, as #6 stretched its fuel to go longer. #6 made its first stop as the safety car came out and handed the lead to #1, with #16 taking the opportunity to make its 2nd stop under the safety car. Into the 3rd hour and #6 took the lead before another safety car, #1 pitted and #6 second guessed itself, losing the lead as it followed #1 in. #16 also stopped and took fuel only to cycle to the lead. #6 then spun on the restart before pitting again, before stopping on track with a gearbox issue. That triggered another safety car, and as the race restarted around the half way point #16 spun and collided, sustaining damage and triggering another safety car as #1 took the lead. As the race entered the 5th hour #1 stopped, but #16 stayed out and rejoined the lead lap, and another safety car allowed the Dyson to catch up. #16 then caught #1 and took the lead late in the 5th hour. The Dyson made its final stop early in the final hour, with #1 stopping a few laps later and cycled to the lead after taking fuel only. Drama in the final stages as #16 stopped on track with an engine issue, bringing out another safety car and allowed #1 to cruise home to take the win.

    Pole Position: #3 Peugeot Sport Total, Peugeot 908 HDi FAP, Pedro Lamy(POR), Sebastien Bourdais(FRA), Simon Pagenaud(FRA), 3.19,711
    Overall Winner: #9 Audi Sport North America, Audi R15 TDI Plus, Timo Bernhard(DEU), Romain Dumas(FRA), Mike Rockenfeller(DEU), 24:01.23,694
    LMP2 Winner: #42 Strakka Racing, HPD ARX-01c, Danny Watts(GBR), Jonny Kane(GBR), Nick Leventis(GBR), +30 Laps

    Peugeot locked out the top 4 in qualifying with the 3 factory cars followed by the Oreca car, with the 3 Audis following. #3 Peugeot controlled the start as #7 Audi moved into 5th and tried to pressure #4 Oreca Peugeot for 4th as #2 Peugeot took 2nd from #1. An early safety car saw the Peugeots and Audis split with the Audis ending up half a lap behind. #4 made its first stop for a splash before the restart. The leaders made their first stop around the hour mark, with #2 Peugeot taking the lead ahead of #3 and #1. The Peugeots traded places for the lead but #2 still lead by the time the leaders made their 2nd stop. As the leaders cycled through the pits in the 3rd hour #3 Peugeot suffered a suspension failure and retired after returning to the garage. #2 continued to hold the lead with #1 now 2nd ahead of #4. The leaders cycled through the pits around the 4h mark, with #1 taking the lead from #2. Into the 5th hour and drama for #7 Audi as it went off trying to avoid another car limping back with a puncture. The car was towed out and limped back to the garage for repairs, leaving #9 in 4th. A long stop in the 6th hour for #9 to replace a mirror following an incident in the pits earlier but maintained 4th ahead of #8. Safety car at the 6h mark saw #1 and #2 split with #1 ending up with a 2 min lead. Meanwhile #8 took 4th from #9 before pitting at the end of the 7th hour. Drama in the 8th hour as #1 pitted and went into the garage with alternator failure, dropping to 7th as #2 took over the lead ahead of #4 and #8. #9 Audi moved back to 3rd as they cycled through the pits around the end of the 9th hour. #1 Peugeot was fighting to recover after the earlier problem, but it went off in the 11th hour after being caught out in traffic and had to be rescued out. Just before the 12 hour mark #4 pitted and went into the garage with a driveshaft failure, leaving #9 2nd ahead of #8 with #2 Peugeot still leading comfortably. Shortly after and into the 13th hour #8 suffered a puncture on the out lap, having to pit again but maintained 3rd. Drama just after the 16 hour mark as the leading #2 Peugeot retired with engine failure, #9 Audi took over the lead ahead of #8 and the recovering #1 Peugeot. Later in the same hour #007 Aston went into the garage from 6th overall with gearbox issues. #1 started pushing hard and in the process tangled in traffic, sending the GT2 leader off. Into the 21st hour and #8 went off and hit the wall, limping back to the pits for a new nose before rejoining, #1 Peugeot now right behind and took 2nd at the end of the hour before pitting. The drama continued as late in the 22nd hour #1 Peugeot suffered an engine failure and retired from 2nd. Audi now 1-2-3 with #9 leading from #8 and #7 but the remaining #4 still catching, however it too suffered an engine failure with just over an hour to go. Aston Martin looked to pick up the pieces from the disintegrating Peugeots, but early in the final hour #009 retired with an engine failure and #007 were slowed with a puncture. That left Audi to dominate the podium with #9 taking the win ahead of #8 and #7.

    Pole Position: #1 Patron Highcroft Racing, HPD ARX-01c, David Brabham(AUS), Simon Pagenaud(FRA), 0.58,106
    Overall Winner: #6 Muscle Milk Team Cytosport, Porsche RS Spyder Evo, Klaus Graf(DEU), Greg Pickett(USA), 2:45.04,386
    PC Winner: #99 Green Earth Team Gunnar, Oreca FLM09 - Chevrolet, Gunnar Jeanette(USA), Elton Julian(USA), +9 Laps

    GTC Winner: #63 TRG, Porsche 997 GT3 Cup, Andy Lally(USA), Henri Richard(FRA), +19 Laps
    #1 Acura qualified on pole ahead of #6 Cytosport Porsche and #16 Dyson in a wet qualifying. As the race started #1 was swamped with #16 taking the lead ahead of #8 Drayson and #37 Intersport. #16 Dyson slowed and pitted with engine issues early in the race, handing the lead to #8 and retiring in the garage. #37 then tangled in traffic and had to pit with damaged suspension as the safety car came out. As the race restarted #8 stopped on track with electrical issues, however the car got going again as another safety car came out and #1 took over the lead ahead of #6. After the restart #6 tangled in traffic but continued as #8 suffered more electrical issues and continued dropping down the order. Another safety car late in the opening hour saw #6 make its first stop, with the leading #1 yet to stop. Over the 2nd stint #6 started catching #1 and took the lead as #1 made its only stop of the race. #6 made its 2nd stop shortly after and maintained the lead as the race approached 2 hours. #1 was trying to catch up, and after initially struggling in heavy traffic started catching rapidly as they battled through a small rainshower. As #1 caught #6 for the lead they made contact navigating traffic, with #1 suffering a puncture and #6 was handed a stop/go for the incident. However with #1 limping around #6 was able to serve the penalty and rejoin ahead to take the win as #1 rescued 2nd.

As the race entered its 5th hour #40 pitted and handed the lead back to #42, which cruised home to take the win with #40 coming home 2nd ahead of #24.

    Pole Position: #07 Team Peugeot Total, Peugeot 908 HDi FAP, Marc Gene(ESP), Alexander Wurz(AUT), Anthony Davidson(GBR), 1.07,187
    Overall Winner: #08 Team Peugeot Total, Peugeot 908 HDi FAP, Pedro Lamy(POR), Stephane Sarrazin(FRA), Franck Montagny(FRA), 9:10.43,451

A safety car in the opening hour saw The Audis and #07 Peugeot make their first stop, with #08 staying out and maintaining the lead. #7 rejoined in 2nd ahead of sister #9 as #07 dropped to 4th. #08 made its first stop as the race entered its 2nd hour, handing the lead to #7. However #08 cycled back to the lead as the others made their 2nd stop later in the 2nd hour. As the race entered its 3rd hour #9 Audi had a close call, going off the track avoiding another car and lost 2nd to #07 as it rejoined across the grass. More problems for #9 as it hit a kerb later in the 3rd hour and suffered a lot of damage to the nose and floor, the car limped back to the pits and went into the garage as the safety car came out. Another safety car later in the 4th hour saw the leaders pit with #7 taking the lead as #08 was delayed in a congested pit lane. Another safety car in the 5th hour saw #08 stay out and take the lead as #7 and #07 stopped, the latter rejoining in 2nd. Into the 7th hour and #7 lost pace, dropping behind #08 before stopping out of sequence for a driver change. The car rejoined a lap down to the leading Peugeots. As the race entered its 8th hour another safety car saw #08 pit from the lead, but #07 stayed out and kept #7 a lap down. #07 and #7 gradually cycled throught their stops with #08 ending up back in front. From there #08 Peugeot controlled the closing hours to take the win ahead of #07, with #7 Audi finishing 3rd after a late puncture a few laps from the end.

The Audi then started catching the leading #2 Peugeot, meanwhile #1 was dropping back and coming under pressure from #8 until the 2nd Audi pitted early in the 4th hour. #7 stopped shortly after before continuing at a scorching pace. #2 stopped later in the same hour, leaving #1 leading but under pressure from #7 which took the lead shortly after. #1 then lost 2nd to sister #2 before making its next stop late in the 4th hour. That left #7 in the lead ahead of #2, until the Peugeot went off the road and lost time going across the gravel. #7 pitted at the start of the 5th hour, #8 following it a few laps later. #2 made its next stop 15 min later and handed the lead back to #7, and drama shortly after as #1 tangled in traffic and limped back to the garage with damage. A brief safety car allowed #2 to close the gap to the leading #7, which made its final stop at the end of the 5th hour. #2 stopped for the final time and rejoined ahead of #7, which had been held up by #1 which was 3 laps down after the earlier incident. #2 Peugeot thus cruised to the finish ahead of #7 Audi, with sister #8 completing the podium.

2011 Season

Overview:

The ACO updated the technical regulations for 2011, focusing on downsizing the engines and making the cars more efficient. The new rules also enabled hybrid systems like the ones seen in F1.
Audi revealed a new car for the new regulations. The team entered the 2nd season of the ILMC, but the R18 wasn't ready for Sebring, with the team entering the old R15s.
Peugeot too revealed a new car for 2011, the 908. Like Audi, the team once again entered the ILMC.
Aston Martin launched their new car for 2011 in the form of the AMR-One. Like Audi and Peugeot, the aim was the ILMC but the car would debut at the LMS opener at Paul Ricard.
After going into administration in 2010 a group of people led by Jacques Nicolet from Oak Racing purchased the assets of Pescarolo Sport when it was auctioned off, and handed it back to Henri Pescarolo. The Pescarolo Team rose from the ashes and brought their 01 Evos up to spec to run 1 car in the LMS.
Highcroft went into 2011 continuing the partnership with HPD, planning to run the latest evolution of the ARX-01, now in LMP1-spec.
With Acura withdrawing after 2009 and HPD continuing the program, for 2011 they continued their partnership with Strakka Racing in Europe, as well as forming a new partnership with RML. However following the earthquake in Japan Highcroft was forced to abandon the partnership, withdrawing from the rest of the season due to financial reasons.
ALMS released an updated calendar for 2011, with Utah dropping off and a race in Baltimore coming in. Another race was planned in Oklahoma City, but the local government voted against funding the race. ALMS also announced changes to the class structure, moving back to separate LMP1 and LMP2 classes as they did before 2010.
LMS revealed a new calendar for 2011, with new races at Imola and Estoril, with the races now running to 6 hours. LMS also announced class changes with LMGT1 phased out, and LMGT2 becoming LMGTE-Pro and LMGTE-Am.
The ILMC released an expanded calendar for 2011, sharing Sebring and Petit Le Mans with ALMS, Spa, Imola and Silverstone with the LMS, and the 24h of Le Mans becoming part of the championship. Zhuhai again closed the season.

2023 Season

Overview:

3 years after the announcement of the convergence between the top class in IMSA and FIA/ACO, the new LMDh cars debuted in the GTP class, marking the first time since 2013 and the ALMS-days that the top class was shared between the European and American premier sportscar championships.
BMW returned for the first time since 2000 with the new M Hybrid V8, for the first year racing with 2 cars in IMSA together with team RLL.
Porsche announced its return to the top class since 2017, revealing the 963 and partnering with Penske Motorsport to run 2 cars in IMSA and 2 cars in the FIA WEC.
Cadillac debuted the V-Series.R to race in both IMSA and WEC, with Chip Ganassi Racing operating 1 car in WEC and one in IMSA, with Action Express Racing operating a second car in IMSA.
Acura launched the ARX-06 for a full season in IMSA with 2 cars operated by Wayne Taylor Racing, which also announced a partnership with Andretti Autosport, and Meyer Shank Racing.
Ferrari returned to the top class for the first time in 50 years with the new 499P, Joining the WEC with 2 cars operated by AF Corse.
After 2 years of testing the ByKolles Vanwall project finally made it onto the FIA WEC grid, despite legal issues with the Vanwall brand still hanging over the team.
After debuting half way through 2022, Peugeot went into its first full season in the WEC, joining Toyota and Glickenhaus along with the newcomers in a record entry in the top class.
Isotta Fraschini also launced a new LMH, but with a very short timeline they were rejected from a full season entry in the WEC. The team initially targeted a debut mid-way through the season, but eventually decided to focus on testing in order to debut in 2024.
With Porsche and Ferrari both focusing on their Hypercar/GTP programs, resulting in potentially only Corvette running in GTE-Pro, the FIA and ACO decided to end the class at the end of 2022, leaving GTE-Am as the only GT class in the WEC for 2023.
WEC started a gradual expansion after conservative seasons following COVID-19, keeping the races from 2022 and adding a race in Portugal, having previously been there in 2021.
IMSA made a few changes to their calendar, dropping Mid-Ohio and Detroit and adding a new event at Indianapolis.

  2. Rolex 24 at Daytona
    Daytona International Speedway, Daytona Beach, Florida
    Date: 28-29.01.2023
    Series: IMSA
    Race Format: 24 Hours
    Classes: GTP, LMP2, LMP3, GTD Pro, GTD
    Circuit Length: 5.729 km
    Laps Completed: 783
    Distance Covered: 4485.807 km
    Number of cars entered: 61 (9 GTP, 10 LMP2, 9 LMP3, 10 GTD Pro, 23 GTD)
    Number of cars finished: 45 (8 GTP, 7 LMP2, 5 LMP3, 8 GTD Pro, 17 GTD)
    Pole Position: #60 Meyer Shank Racing, Acura ARX-06, Tom Blomqvist(GBR), Colin Braun(USA), Helio Castroneves(BRA), Simon Pagenaud(FRA), 1.34,031
    Overall Winner: #60 Meyer Shank Racing, Acura ARX-06, Tom Blomqvist(GBR), Colin Braun(USA), Helio Castroneves(BRA), Simon Pagenaud(FRA), 24:01.19,952
    LMP2 Winner: #55 Proton Competition, Oreca 07 - Gibson, Gianmaria Bruni(ITA), James Allen(AUS), Francesco Pizzi(ITA), Fred Poordad(USA), +22 Laps
    LMP3 Winner: #17 AWA, Duqueine D08 - Nissan, Wayne Boyd(GBR), Nicolas Varrone(ARG), Anthony Mantella(CAN), Thomas Merrill(USA), +46 Laps
    GTD Winner: #27 Heart of Racing Team, Aston Martin Vantage AMR GT3, Marco Sørensen(DEN), Darren Turner(GBR), Roman De Angelis(CAN), Ian James(GBR), +54 Laps
    GTD Pro Winner: #79 WeatherTech Racing, Mercedes-AMG GT3 Evo, Maro Engel(DEU), Jules Gounon(FRA), Daniel Juncadella(ESP), Cooper MacNeil(USA), +54 Laps
    #60 Acura led the early stages with the #25 BMW hitting trouble less than an hour in with a hybrid issue, spending several hours in the garage. #01 Cadillac briefly took the lead when the #60 Acura had to make several pit stops under a safety car period 2 hour in, changing the tail after suffering rear wing damage. However the Acura re-took the lead with a faster stop under another safety car an hour later. #7 Porsche also suffered a hybrid issue around the 6 hour mark, losing several laps changing the battery in the garage. Throughout the night the Acuras developed issues with the oil system, #10 requiring a short trip to the garage to replace the oil filter and oil filler cap. The #60 was having similar issues, having to make several pit stops to manage the issue while staying withing touching distance of the lead lap. As Sunday morning approached the #31 Cadillac slowed and went into the garage with broken suspension after contact, dropping several laps down. Soon after the remaining #6 Porsche spun off, suffering rear damage and dropping out of the lead battle as it pitted for repairs. Throughout Sunday morning the BMWs suffered more issues, #25 with a minor gearbox issue and #24 had brake issues requiring a visit to the garage. The #7 Porsche also suffered a broken water pipe, costing more laps. Drama as the #6 Porsche suffered a gearbox failure 3 hours from the end, stopping on track with smoke coming out of the rear, retiring after getting back to the pits on electric power. The fight for the win was mainly contested by the #60 Acura and the #01 and #02 Cadillacs, however with a series of safety cars in the closing hours, the #10 Acura went from 2 laps down to the lead lap, and it soon took the Cadillacs for 2nd, however the #60 Acura held on in the closing stages to take the win.

  3. 1000 Miles of Sebring
    Sebring International Raceway, Sebring, Florida
    Date: 17.03.2023
    Series: WEC
    Race Format: 1000 Miles or 8 Hours
    Classes: Hypercar, LMP2, LMGTE-Am
    Circuit Length: 6.019 km
    Laps Completed: 239
    Distance Covered: 1438.541 km
    Number of cars entered: 37 (11 Hypercar, 12 LMP2, 14 LMGTE-Am)
    Number of cars finished: 31 (9 Hypercar, 10 LMP2, 12 LMGTE-Am)
    Pole Position: #50 Ferrari AF Corse, Ferrari 499P, Antonio Fuoco(ITA), Miguel Molina(ESP), Nicklas Nielsen(DEN), 1.45,067
    Overall Winner: #7 Toyota Gazoo Racing, Toyota GR010 Hybrid, Mike Conway(GBR), Kamui Kobayashi(JAP), Jose Maria Lopez(ARG), 8:00.19,877
    LMP2 Winner: #48 Hertz Team Jota, Oreca 07 - Gibson, Yifei Ye(CHN), Will Stevens(GBR), David Beckmann(DEU), +9 Laps
    LMGTE-Am Winner: #33 Corvette Racing, Chevrolet Corvette C8.R, Nicky Catsburg(NED), Nicolas Varrone(ARG), Ben Keating(USA), +18 Laps
    #50 Ferrari led from pole as #94 Peugeot suffered a gearbox failure on the formation lap and went straight to the garage. An early SC saw the two Ferraris pit for fuel, leaving the Toyotas in the lead. On the restart #708 Glickenhaus stopped on track with electrical issues, eventually getting going again. 1h into the race #93 Peugeot also suffered a gearbox failure and dropped down the order as it went to the garage. As the leaders made their first stop the Ferraris briefly cycled back to the front until they made their 2nd stop. The battle for 3rd towards the end of the 2nd stint was fierce between #6 Porsche and #2 Cadillac, the Porsche struggling on worn tyres. #94 suffered a hybrid issue and pulled into the garage and retired. #7 Toyota led until the 2nd stop, where #8 stayed out 2 more laps and came out ahead. #708 suffered more electrical issues and stopped on track, retiring from the race. Contact between #93 Peugeot and #4 Vanwall near the 3h mark as the FCY came out, #93 spinning and #4 having to pit with bodywork damage. As another FCY came out #8 Toyota was about to pit from the lead, but could only take emergency fuel as the pits were closed, having to come in again when the race went back to green, however it kept the lead. However it later lost the lead as it was saving fuel, dropping behind #7. Drama at the 6h mark as #51 Ferrari had contact in traffic, crashing out and suffering a puncture and substantial rear damage, dropping several laps down while in the garage. Vanwall had a steady race, until a suspension failure in the 7th hour, it too spending time in the garage fixing the damage. #7 cruised home to take the win ahead of sister #8, with #50 finishing 3rd

  4. Mobil 1 Twelve Hours of Sebring
    Sebring International Raceway, Sebring, Florida
    Date: 18.03.2023
    Series: IMSA
    Race Format: 12 Hours
    Classes: GTP, LMP2, LMP3, GTD Pro, GTD
    Circuit Length: 6.019 km
    Laps Completed: 322
    Distance Covered: 1938.118 km
    Number of cars entered: 54 (8 GTP, 8 LMP2, 10 LMP3, 8 GTD Pro, 20 GTD)
    Number of cars finished: 39 (3 GTP, 6 LMP2, 7 LMP3, 8 GTD Pro, 15 GTD)
    Pole Position: #31 Action Express Racing, Cadillac V-Series.R, Luis Felipe Derani(BRA), Alexander Sims(GBR), Jack Aitken(GBR), 1.45,836
    Overall Winner: #31 Action Express Racing, Cadillac V-Series.R, Luis Felipe Derani(BRA), Alexander Sims(GBR), Jack Aitken(GBR), 12:00.53,382
    LMP2 Winner: #8 Tower Motorsports, Oreca 07 - Gibson, Kyffin Simpson(BAR), Scott McLaughlin(NZE), John Farano(CAN), +4 Laps
    LMP3 Winner: #74 Riley Motorsports, Ligier JS P320 - Nissan, Felipe Fraga(BRA), Josh Burdon(AUS), Gar Robinson(USA), +13 Laps
    GTD Pro Winner: #9 Pfaff Motorsports, Porsche 911 GT3 R (992), Klaus Bachler(AUT), Patrick Pilet(FRA), Laurens Vanthoor(BEL), +19 Laps
    GTD Winner: #1 Paul Miller Racing, BMW M4 GT3, Corey Lewis(USA), Bryan Sellers(USA), Madison Snow(USA), +21 Laps
    #31 Cadillac led the opening stages as #01 Cadillac and #10 Acura traded places in the first stint, before #01 took the lead at the first stop. A safety car restart during the 2nd stint saw #31 struggle on old tyres, dropping down the order until it had contact with a spinning car and then scattering debris everywhere trying to stay out before being forced to come in. When the leaders pitted #10 took the lead, but trying to double stint tyres it dropped down the order leaving #01 back in front. #6 Porsche suffered early issues, first diagnosing a hydraulic issue under the safety car, and then a puncture 3h in cost it time. During the 4th hour #24 BMW went off and suffered damage, and #6 slowed on track with fumes in the cockpit, as #7 Porsche suffered suspension issues and pitted for repairs. #01 had built a substantial lead, but a safety car at the 5h mark wiped it out with #10 taking the lead after pitting just before, with the rest stopping when the pit lane opened. #31 made it back to the lead lap, and traded places multiple times with #01 for 2nd overall until another SC, at which point #24 BMW stopped on track and retired with overheating. After the restart #01 struggled on old tyres and dropped from 2nd to 7th, as a bizarre incident under SC at the 7h mark saw an LMP3 car unlapping itself hit the rear of #6, both cars suffering damage. #31 took the lead as the leaders cycled through the pits, with #10 penalized for speeding. After a safety car during the 9th hour #01 muscled its way into the lead, with #10 following it into 2nd, dropping #31 to 3rd, however at the 9h mark #01 pitted from the lead and retired with engine failure. More drama with less than 2h to go as #60 Acura lost a wheel and stopped on track. The leaders pitted in anticipation of the SC, leaving #25 in the lead until it stopped when the pits opened and changed the brakes, with #6 taking tyres. On the restart #6 Porsche on new tyres took 3rd from #31, and after another SC restart with 1h to go it took 2nd from #7, pressuring #10 for the lead, banging wheels. #31 made its final stop, with #7 pitting to serve a penalty for a pit stop infringement as another SC came out. When the pits opened #10 and #6 made their final stop, with #7 also pitting for new tyres. On the restart #6 again went aggressive and took the lead, with #31 shuffled from the lead to 4th, until with 18 min to go #6 was baulked in traffic, contact with #10 ending in both cars crashing out, #7 failing to avoid it with all three cars eliminated. That left #31 leading ahead of #25, and they controlled the pace as the race restarted with 5min left to take the win

  5. Acura Grand Prix of Long Beach
    Long Beach Street Circuit, Long Beach, California
    Date: 15.04.2023
    Series: IMSA
    Race Format: 1 Hour 40 minutes
    Classes: GTP, GTD Pro, GTD
    Circuit Length: 3.167 km
    Laps Completed: 78
    Distance Covered: 247.026 km
    Number of cars entered: 28 (8 GTP, 5 GTD Pro, 15 GTD)
    Number of cars finished: 24 (6 GTP, 5 GTD Pro, 13 GTD)
    Pole Position: #10 Wayne Taylor Racing, Acura ARX-06, Ricky Taylor(USA), Felipe Albuquerque(POR), 1.09,909
    Overall Winner: #6 Porsche Penske Motorsports, Porsche 963, Mathieu Jaminet(FRA), Nick Tandy(GBR), 1:42.08,126
    GTD Pro Winner: #14 Vasser Sullivan Racing, Lexus RC F GT3, Ben Barnicoat(GBR), Jack Hawksworth(GBR), +5 Laps
    GTD Winner: #1 Paul Miller Racing, BMW M4 GT3, Bryan Sellers(USA), Madison Snow(USA), +5 Laps
    The two Acuras locked out the front row, as #01 Cadillac spun and crashed at the start, with #60 Acura also spinning after contact with #25 BMW. #10 Acura led the early stages ahead of #6 Porsche and the two BMWs. #31 Cadillac made a very early stop just 15 min in, dropping almost a lap down. As the leaders made their only stop of the race, #10 went from the lead to 5th after being delayed at its stop, with the Porsches ending up 1st and 3rd after not taking tyres. #31 Cadillac pitted from 2nd for its 2nd stop with 30 min to go, leaving #7 Porsche 2nd under massive pressure on old tyres, first from #25 BMW until it went off, then the #10 Acura. After enormous pressure #10 Acura took 2nd, with #25 following it through having also re-joined the battle with the #7. #10 quickly caught the leading #6 and tried to take the lead with just 2 laps to go, but braked too late and crashed out, leaving #6 Porsche to take the win

  6. 6 Hours of Portimao
    Algarve International Circuit, Portimao, Portugal
    Date: 16.04.2023
    Series: WEC
    Race Format: 6 Hours
    Classes: Hypercar, LMP2, LMGTE-Am
    Circuit Length: 4.653 km
    Laps Completed: 222
    Distance Covered: 1032.966 km
    Number of cars entered: 37 (11 Hypercar, 12 LMP2, 14 LMGTE-Am)
    Number of cars finished: 35 (10 Hypercar, 12 LMP2, 13 LMGTE-Am)
    Pole Position: #8 Toyota Gazoo Racing, Toyota GR010 Hybrid, Sebastien Buemi(CHE), Brendon Hartley(NZE), Ryo Hirakawa(JAP), 1.30,171
    Overall Winner: #8 Toyota Gazoo Racing, Toyota GR010 Hybrid, Sebastien Buemi(CHE), Brendon Hartley(NZE), Ryo Hirakawa(JAP), 6:01.26,343
    LMP2 Winner: #23 United Autosports, Oreca 07 - Gibson, Giedo van der Garde(NED), Oliver Jarvis(GBR), Josh Pierson(USA), +7 Laps
    LMGTE-Am Winner: #33 Corvette Racing, Chevrolet Corvette C8.R, Nicky Catsburg(NED), Nicolas Varrone(ARG), Ben Keating(USA), +16 Laps
    Toyota locked out the front row, with #7 taking an early lead and #51 Ferrari briefly in 2nd until #8 re-took the place. #93 Peugeot started from the pit lane after having to change the steering column before the race. The two Ferraris argued over track position in the first stint, with #50 eventually getting ahead, with the two Toyotas too swapping places before the end of the first stint. As the cars cycled through the first stops, both #6 Porsche and #2 Cadillac jumped the two ferraris by not taking tyres, however both cars struggled in the second stint, with #2 having to stop again after suffering with a flat spot. Drama in the 2nd hour as #7 Toyota pitted from 2nd with a problem with a driveshaft torque sensor, the team forced to stop and change the parts, losing 7 laps. Problems also hit #51 Ferrari in the 3rd hour, suffering problems with the front braking system and having to make an extra stop to help the brake cooling. #5 Porsche slowed on track and pitted at the 4h mark, but after rejoining seemingly without problems it came back in shortly after with a power steering failure and dropped out of contention. #4 Vanwall suffered a brake failure and crashed out just before the 5h mark, bringing out the safety car. In the final hour #51 suffered a brake failure too, and slowed dramatically to nurse the car to the end. #6 Porsche looked set for 3rd place until it had to make a late splash of fuel to make it to the end, however it managed to hang on to finish ahead of the #2 Cadillac which finished 4th after running off sequence since the tyre issues earlier in the race. Meanwhile #8 Toyota went unchallenged to take the win ahead of the #50 Ferrari

  7. TotalEnergies 6 Hours of Spa-Franchorchamps
    Circuit de Spa-Franchorchamps, Stavelot, Belgium
    Date: 29.04.2023
    Series: WEC
    Race Format: 6 Hours
    Classes: Hypercar, LMP2, LMGTE-Am
    Circuit Length: 7.004 km
    Laps Completed: 148
    Distance Covered: 1036.592 km
    Number of cars entered: 38 (13 Hypercar, 11 LMP2, 14 LMGTE-Am)
    Number of cars finished: 31 (9 Hypercar, 10 LMP2, 12 LMGTE-Am)
    Pole Position: #7 Toyota Gazoo Racing, Toyota GR010 Hybrid, Mike Conway(GBR), Kamui Kobayashi(JAP), Jose Maria Lopez(ARG), 2.00,812
    Overall Winner: #7 Toyota Gazoo Racing, Toyota GR010 Hybrid, Mike Conway(GBR), Kamui Kobayashi(JAP), Jose Maria Lopez(ARG), 6:00.24,798
    LMP2 Winner: #41 Team WRT, Oreca 07 - Gibson, Robert Kubica(POL), Louis Deletraz(CHE), Rui Andrade(ANG), +2 Laps
    LMGTE-Am Winner: #83 Richard Mille AF Corse, Ferrari 488 GTE Evo, Alessio Rovera(ITA), Lilou Wadoux(FRA), Luis Perez Companc(ARG), +8 Laps
    The race started in damp and cold conditions, with half the cars starting on slicks and half on wets. After multiple spins and cars struggling to keep pace with the safety car an extra formation lap was added. #7 Toyota started on pole, but fell back on slicks along with #3 Cadillac and the Porsches. The wet-shod two Ferraris led the early stages ahead of #2 Cadillac, until an early safety car, at which point the track had dried enough that the slick runners could catch back up. #7 Toyota re-took the lead followed by #6 Porsche as the wet runners all pitted. Once on slicks, the two Ferraris struggled heavily to get up to temperature, haemorrhaging time and going a lap down. #5 Porsche and #8 Toyota gradually made their way towards the front, #8 having started at the back after an accident in qualifying. #6 Porsche lost time during the first pit cycle, falling behind #3 Cadillac and #8 Toyota as #7 maintained the lead, however #8 suffering on worn tyres fell back behind #6. Drama in the 2nd hour as #3 Cadillac suffered a heavy accident after a power steering failure, the car retiring with the driver sent to the medical centre. #6 Porsche was holding a strong 2nd place until a complete electrical failure saw the car stop on track and retire, as at the same time #4 Vanwall went off and got stuck in the gravel. Problems continued for #4 Vanwall, after briefly stopping on track before driving back slowly to close the door in the 4th hour, it got tangled up in traffic and crashed out of the race. After pitting in the 5th hout #50 Ferrari exited the pit lane and immediately crashed out on cold tyres, it too retiring from the race. #7 Toyota controlled the lead through the final stints despite late pressure from sister #8, including a 5 second penalty for overtaking off the track. #5 Porsche was set for 3rd place until #51 Ferrari hunted it down and took the place on the final lap
