    Ferrari locked out the front row ahead of #8 Toyota and #75 Porsche, but #708 Glickenhaus was forced to start from the pits after a gearbox leak on the way to the grid. #50 Ferrari led away from pole, but struggled on a wet section of track after earlier rain, and #8 Toyota took the lead on the first lap as #311 Cadillac crashed and brought out the safety car. The car returned to the pits with heavy damage and went several laps down. On the restart #7 Toyota took 2nd from #50 Ferrari, but as the Toyotas struggled on their softer tyres #50 re-took 3rd before making its first stop. #7 Toyota struggled, losing 3rd to #51 and coming under pressure from the trio of Porsches. The rest of the leaders made their first stop with #8 maintaining the lead. As cars gradually cycled through their second stops several cars took turns leading, with #2 Cadillac in front at the 2h mark. #3 Cadillac was involved in an accident after being collected while slowing for a slow zone, returning to the garage and going laps down. The lead continued to change hands as cars were cycling through stops at various rates due to the amount of slow zones. #6 Porsche hit problems in the 3rd hour, losing time with a puncture and dropping a lap down. Rain started falling as the race approached 3 hours, and as it intensified conditions became undrivable, with #3 Cadillac and #709 Glickenhaus aquaplaning off. The safety car was deployed due to the conditions, and the leaders all pitted for wets. Once the pit stops had cycled through it was #94 Peugeot leading, with #38 Jota 2nd. After spending a hour under safety car the track had started to dry again, with some of the cars moving back to slicks before the restart. #93 Peugeot went off after stopping for slicks and got stuck in the gravel. As the race restarted #94 still led from #6 Porsche and #7 Toyota, but all three soon stopped for slicks. That left #38 Jota in the lead ahead of #5 Porsche, but the two Ferraris were moving up the order and relegated #5 to 4th as #6 Porsche suffered another puncture. #38 controlled the lead until dramatically crashing out approaching the 5h mark, bringing the car back with substantial damage, triggering an FCY to clear the debris. By this point Ferrari had taken control of the race, #51 leading until a swap with #50 to effectivise pit stops, however #51 was back in front by the next stop. #709 Glickenhaus suffered more issues, a loose wheel dragging under the car costing a lot of time by the time it made it back to the pits. Heavy rain started falling again in the 7th hour, with trecherous conditions causing several cars to aquaplane off. Everyone pitted for wets, with #51 Ferrari maintaining the lead ahead of #94 and #7 after #2 Cadillac spun off in the awful conditions. #75 Porsche stopped on track towards the end of the 7th hour, eventually bringing the car back to the pits and retiring with fuel pressure issues. As the rain eased the leaders gradually pitted for slicks, #51 Ferrari still leading ahead of #94 Peugeot and #7 Toyota. #4 Vanwall was having a miserable race, including an off into the gravel in the 8th hour. Drama as #51 Ferrari went off from the lead into the gravel just before the 8h mark, handing the lead to #94 Peugeot ahead of #7 Toyota and #50 Ferrari. Just a few moments later more drama as #7 Toyota was involved in an accident, getting collected while slowing for a slow zone and suffering two punctures and a broken driveshaft, retiring from the race. The order was #94 Peugeot in the lead ahead of #50 Ferrari and #2 Cadillac as first an FCY and then a safety car was deployed to clear up the accident. With more pit cycles in the 9th hour #50 lost time in the pits, with #8 Toyota taking 2nd ahead of #2 Cadillac. As the race restarted #8 Toyota took the lead until its next stop, as #5 Porsche went into the garage in the 10th hour with hybrid cooling issues, dropping down the order. At the end of the hour #50 Ferrari also went ito the garage with a water leak, dropping several laps down. By the time #94 had made its next stop #8 Toyota was back on its tail and took the lead in the 11th hour, with #51 Ferrari having come back to demote #94 to 3rd. #94 Peugeot then crashed in the 12th hour, dropping out of the podium fight as it brought the car back to the pits with heavy front end damage. That left #51 Ferrari with a narrow lead as the race reached half way, after taking the lead in the pits when #8 Toyota took full service. As the pit cycles continued #51 Ferrari had its full service stop at its next stop, leaving #8 back out front in the 13th hour. As dawn broke #4 Vanwall suffered an engine failure and retired in the 16th hour, capping off a miserable race. After an impact with a squirrel caused damage to the front splitter #8 Toyota started losing pace as the race approached 16 hours, and a slow puncture meant #51 Ferrari took the lead at the next stop with a nose change and new tyre for the Toyota. Around the same time #3 Cadillac had moved into 4th with #6 Porsche serving a penalty. Trying to catch back up #6 went off after tangling in traffic, going into the garage at the next stop with floor damage. #708 Glickenhaus spun off into the wall in the 17th hour, with #709 going off in the same place an hour later, both cars forced to visit the garage for quick repairs. Meanwhile #94 Peugeot also went into the garage quickly to check the oil temperature. #51 Ferrari continued to hold the advantage throughout the morning until a slow pit stop just after the 18h mark, with the car failing to start and requiring a power cycle. #8 Toyota took the lead, however #51 fought back to re-take the lead on track later in the 19th hour. Problems continued for #6 Porsche, with another visit to the garage with hybrid issues in the 19th hour, followed by another stop an hour later to replace the battery system. Meanwhile #311 Cadillac went off into the gravel after slowly moving up the order after the first lap crash. As the race moved into the 21st hour the Peugeots hit problems, with #94 going into the garage to replace the steering rack, and #93 replacing the nose after a nose panel flew off before being forced to come in again with hydraulic issues. With 2 hours to go #8 Toyota was starting to catch the leading #51 Ferrari, but drama as the car went off and hit the wall in the penultimate hour, falling almost a lap down after pitting for new nose and tail. That left #51 Ferrari with a comfortable lead, and controlled the final stages to win the race despite a long final stop with another power cycle. #8 Toyota came home 2nd, with #2 Cadillac taking 3rd after a near problem-free race. #5 Porsche suffered late gearbox issues, spending the last half hour in the garage, with #709 Glickenhaus also going off and getting stuck in the gravel in the final hour.

The resulting safety car saw #01 pit for repairs, and after the restart #24 also pitted with a slow puncture and a few laps later with electrical issues, leaving #25 in 3rd. Confusion as another safety car saw the leaders make their first stop late in the opening hour. #6 maintained the lead through the stop, but #31 Cadillac was alongside #7 exiting the stop but had to drop in 3rd. As the cars were reordering for the restart #31 was ordered to take the lead after the Porsches were deemed to have failed to respond to race control in time. #31 thus led the restart as the race entered its 2nd hour, with #7 moving past #6 for 2nd. The Porsches pressured the Cadillac and later in the stint #31 went wide and handed the lead to #7, with #6 also going through. The leaders made their 2nd stop late in the 2nd hour, but #7 went off on the out lap and handed the lead to #6 as #25 BMW rejoined 3rd ahead of #31. #6 Porsche thus controlled the closing stages to take the win ahead of sister #7, with #25 completing the podium.

2024 Season

Overview:

After competing in the Hypercar class in 2021 and 2022 with the rebadged Rebellion LMP1 car, Alpine revealed the new A424-Beta, set to compete in the WEC.
Another newcomer to the top class was Lamborghini, revealing the SC63 and preparing to compete in the WEC as well as the endurance events in IMSA.
After competing in IMSA with Acura in 2023 and following the partnership with Andretti, WTR added a second car to its campaign for 2024. Conversely, after a controversy with tyre pressures at the Rolex 24, Meyer Shank Racing split with Acura at the end of the season. Unable to find other alternatives, the team paused its sportscar program for 2024 to focus on Indycar.
Following the elimination of the GTE-Pro class after 2022, FIA and ACO made further changes to the class structure in the WEC for 2024. The GTE-Am class was phased out and replaced by the LMGT3 class, based on the much more widely used GT3-spec cars. At the same time the increase of entries in the Hypercar class forced the organizer to eliminate the LMP2 class from the FIA WEC, leaving the series with only 2 classes in 2024. LMP2 cars were however still eligible in other ACO supported series like the ELMS, AsLMS and IMSA, as well as at Le Mans.
IMSA also made changes to the class structure for 2024, with the LMP3 class eliminated due to the other classes seing increased interest. The LMP3 class was added in 2021 to fill up the grid at a time when reduced interest caused smaller grids at several events.
The FIA WEC revealed a new calendar for 2024, continuing the gradual expansion following the COVID years. The new calendar featured a new event in Qatar, as well as a return to Interlagos and COTA and a first visit to Imola.
IMSA revealed a revised calendar with a new event in Detroit together with IndyCar replacing Lime Rock, with Indianapolis becoming a 6 hour endurance. The calendar also saw several revisions of which classes competed at which events.

2025 Season

Overview:

Aston Martin confirmed a revival of its hypercar program with the Valkyrie which was originally shelved in 2020. Partnering with The Heart of Racing Team, the car was brought up to the latest spec, with the team planning to race one car each in IMSA and WEC.
